Judge's Ruling on Wala: Tajiz or Not?
Explains effect of judge's ruling on wala of mukatab's child.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a judicial ruling that confirms the kitabah (not tajiz) and one that constitutes a declaration of the mukatab's inability (tajiz) in the context of a child's wala.

Core Idea
A judge's ruling on wala only constitutes tajiz when the dispute directly concerns the validity of the kitabah.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a nuanced scenario: a mukatab dies, leaving a child from a free woman and sufficient debt to pay the kitabah. The child commits a crime, and a judge imposes blood money liability on the mother's 'aqila. Does this ruling declare the mukatab unable (tajiz)? The author explains that it does not, because it confirms the kitabah. However, if the maternal and paternal masters dispute the child's wala and the judge awards it to the maternal masters, that ruling does constitute tajiz. The key is whether the ruling directly addresses the status of the kitabah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage describes two separate judicial rulings involving the same family situation. First: a ruling on who pays blood money for the child's crime. Second: a ruling on who gets the child's wala when disputed.
Focus on the legal effect of each ruling, not the facts.
2
Analyze the first ruling: 'aql on mother's 'aqila
The judge imposes blood money on the mother's agnates. This ruling is not tajiz because it confirms the kitabah contract—the child is attached to the maternal masters only provisionally, pending possible freedom of the mukatab.
The ruling is consistent with the possibility that the mukatab may die free.
3
Analyze the second ruling: wala dispute
If the maternal and paternal masters dispute the child's wala, and the judge awards it to the maternal masters, this ruling is tajiz. Why? Because the dispute itself hinges on whether the kitabah is intact—if dissolved, wala goes to maternal masters; if intact and paid, wala transfers to paternal masters. The judge's decision necessarily decides the status of the kitabah.
The ruling resolves the ambiguity about the kitabah, thus declaring the mukatab 'ajiz.
4
Understand the principle of ijtihad
The author notes this is a matter of ijtihad, meaning the judge's ruling is enforceable even if it might be subject to scholarly disagreement. The key is that the ruling in the second scenario is a definitive declaration of inability because it directly settles the wala dispute.
In Hanafi fiqh, once a judge rules, the matter is final (nafadh).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال فان مات المكاتب وله ولد من حرة وترك دينا وفاء لمكاتبته فجنى الولد فقضى به على عاقلة الام ولم يكن ذلك قضاء بعجز المكاتب لان هذا القضاء يقرر حكم الكتابة لان من قضيتها الحاق الولد بموالي الام و ايجاب العقل عليهم لكن على وجه يحتمل ان يعتق فيجر الولاء الى موالى الاب والقضاء بما يقرر حكمه لا يكون تعجيزا وان اختصم موالى الام وموالى الاب فى ولائه فقضى به لموالى الام فهو قضاء بالعجز لان هذا اختلاف فى الولاء مقصودا و ذلك يبتنى على بقاء الكتابة وانتقاضها فانها اذا فسخت مات عبدا واستقر الولاء على موالى الام واذا بقيت واتصل بها الاداء مات حرا وانتقل الولاء الى موالى الاب وهذا فصل مجتهد فيه فينقذ ما يلاقيه من القضاء فلهذا كان تعجيزا ترجمہ اگر مر گیا مکاتب جس کا کوئی فرزند ہے آزاد عورت سے اور چھوڑ گیا ایسا قرضہ جس سے اس کی کتابت ادا ہو سکتی ہے پھر فرزند نے جنایت کی جس کا حکم عاقلہ ام پر دے دیا گیا تو مکاتب کے عاجز ہونے کا حکم نہ ہوگا کیونکہ یہ قضاء تو حکم کتابت کو مضبوط کرتا ہے اس لئے کہ کتابت کا مقتضی فرزند کو موالی ام کے ساتھ لاحق کرنا اور عقل کو انہیں پر واجب کرنا ہے لیکن اس طور پر جس میں یہ احتمال ہو کہ وہ فرزند آزاد ہو کر ولاء موالی اب کی طرف کھینچ لائے گا اور جو قضاء حکم کتابت کو مضبوط کرے وہ عاجز ٹھہرانا نہیں ہوتا۔ اگر جھگڑا کیا موالی ام اور موالی اب نے فرزند کی ولاء میں او قاضی نے اس کا حکم موالی ام کے لئے دے دیا تو یہ عاجز ہو جانے کا حکم ہے کیونکہ یہ اختلاف ہے ولاء میں بالقصد جو کتابت کے باقی رہنے اور ٹوٹ جانے پر مبنی ہے اس لئے کہ اگر کتابت فسخ ہو جائے تو مکاتب غلام ہو کر مرا اور فرزند کی ولاء موالی ام پر مستعقر ہوگی ۔ اور یہ صورت چونکہ مجتہد فیہ ہے اس لئے جو قضاء اس سے ملاقی ہو وہ نافذ ہو جائے گی اس لئے یہ قضاء اس کے عاجز ہونے کا حکم ہے۔ تشریح قوله فان مات ... الخ ایک مکاتب آزاد عورت سے ایک بیٹا اور لوگوں پر اپنا اتنا قرض چھوڑ کر مر گیا جو بدل کتابت کے
He said: If the mukatab dies and he has a child from a free woman, and leaves a debt sufficient to fulfill his kitabah, then the child commits a crime and a judgment is passed against the 'aqila of the mother, that judgment is not a declaration of the mukatab's inability (tajiz), because this judgment confirms the ruling of kitabah. For part of its requirement is to attach the child to the maternal masters (mawali al-umm) and to impose the 'aql (blood money liability) on them, but in a manner that allows the possibility that the child may become free and then pull the wala to the paternal masters. And a judgment that confirms its ruling is not a tajiz. But if the maternal masters and paternal masters dispute over his wala and the judge rules for the maternal masters, then that is a judgment of inability (tajiz), because this is a specific dispute over wala, and that dispute is based on the continuation or dissolution of the kitabah. For if the kitabah is dissolved, the mukatab dies as a slave and the wala is settled with the maternal masters. And if it continues and payment is made, he dies free and the wala transfers to the paternal masters. And this is a matter subject to ijtihad, so whatever judgment is given will be enforced. Therefore, this is a judgment of inability. Translation: If a mukatab dies and he has a child from a free woman and leaves such a debt that his kitabah can be paid, then the child commits a crime and the judgment of the 'aqila of the mother is given, that is not a judgment of the mukatab's inability, because this judgment strengthens the ruling of kitabah. For the necessary consequence of kitabah is to attach the child to the maternal masters and to make the 'aql obligatory on them, but in a way that there is a possibility that the child may become free and pull the wala to the paternal masters. And a judgment that strengthens its ruling is not a declaration of inability. If the maternal and paternal masters dispute over the child's wala and the judge gives it to the maternal masters, then this is a declaration of inability, because this is a specific dispute over wala based on the continuation or dissolution of the kitabah. For if the kitabah is dissolved, the mukatab dies as a slave and the child's wala is settled with the maternal masters. And this case is subject to ijtihad, so whatever judgment meets it will be enforced. Therefore, this judgment is a declaration of inability. Explanation of the saying 'If he dies...' - A mukatab dies leaving a son from a free woman and a debt on people sufficient to pay the kitabah...
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage presents a specific scenario: a mukatab dies leaving a child from a free wife and enough debt to cover the kitabah. The child commits a crime (jinaya) and the judge imposes the 'aql (blood money liability) on the 'aqila of the mother (the maternal agnates). This ruling does not constitute a declaration of the mukatab's inability (tajiz) because it confirms the kitabah; the judgment attaches the child to the maternal masters temporarily, but with the possibility that the child may become free (if the kitabah is paid) and then the wala (clientage) goes to the paternal masters. However, if the maternal and paternal masters specifically dispute over the child's wala and the judge awards it to the maternal masters, that ruling does constitute tajiz. Why? Because this dispute directly concerns the status of the kitabah: if the kitabah is dissolved (meaning the mukatab died unable to pay), he dies a slave and the child's wala belongs to the maternal masters. If the kitabah remains in effect (and payment is made), the mukatab dies free and the wala transfers to his paternal masters. Since this is a matter of ijtihad, the judge's ruling is final. The lesson emphasizes that not every judicial ruling regarding the child implies the mukatab's inability; only a ruling on a direct dispute over wala between the two sets of masters does so.

Key Terms
عاجز (‘ājiz): Incapable; here, a declaration that the mukatab is unable to pay the kitabah, resulting in his return to slavery.
ولاء (walā’): Clientage; the legal relationship of inheritance and responsibility between a freed slave and his former master.
موالی الام (mawālī al-umm): The masters of the mother; the agnates of the free woman who are responsible for her child's wala and 'aql in certain circumstances.
موالی الاب (mawālī al-ab): The masters of the father; the agnates of the mukatab father who claim wala if the father dies free.
عاقلہ (‘āqilah): The agnatic group responsible for paying blood money (diya) on behalf of a member who commits homicide.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where a mukatab dies with a child from a free woman and sufficient debt for kitabah, what is the effect of a judge's ruling that imposes 'aql on the mother's 'aqila?
A) It is a declaration of the mukatab's inability (tajiz).
B) It confirms the kitabah and is not a declaration of inability.
C) It invalidates the kitabah contract.
D) It frees the child immediately.

Key Takeaway
A judicial ruling only constitutes a declaration of the mukatab's inability (tajiz) when it directly decides the fate of the kitabah, as in a dispute over wala.

Distinguishing Qadi Rulings on Mukatab's 'Ajz via Son's Jinayat
Ruling on whether qadi's judgments determine 'ajz of mukatab in case of son's jinayat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between two types of qadi rulings involving a mukatab's family and state whether each constitutes a judgment of 'ajz.

Core Idea
A qadi's ruling on a mukatab's son's 'aqila does not imply 'ajz; a ruling on wala does.

This lesson explores a nuanced Hanafi ruling from Kitab al-Mukatab. When a mukatab dies, his son's legal status can raise questions about the kitabah contract. The passage distinguishes between two qadi rulings: one that confirms the kitabah and one that dissolves it, with different consequences for 'ajz.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two cases: (a) a qadi ruling on the son's 'aqila, (b) a qadi ruling on the son's wala.
2
Determine the qadi's ruling in each
In scenario (a), the qadi orders the mother's 'aqila to pay; in scenario (b), the qadi awards wala to the mother's masters.
3
Analyze the legal basis for 'ajz
Scenario (a) confirms the kitabah, so no 'ajz; scenario (b) decides the wala dispute, which depends on the kitabah's status, so it constitutes 'ajz.
4
Understand the role of wala
Wala is determined by whether the mukatab died free or a slave, which depends on the kitabah's fulfillment. A direct ruling on wala thus implicitly declares 'ajz.

Source Text

قال فان مات المكاتب وله ولد من حرة وترك دينا وفاء لمكاتبته فجنى الولد فقضى به على عاقلة الام ولم یکن ذلك قضاء بعجز المكاتب لان هذا القضاء يقرر حكم الكتابة لان من قضيتها الحاق الولد بموالي الام و ايجاب العقل عليهم لكن على وجه يحتمل ان يعتق فيجر الولاء الى موالى الاب والقضاء بما يقرر حکمه لا يكون تعجيزا وان اختصم موالى الام وموالى الاب فى ولائه فقضى به لموالى الام فهو قضاء بالعجز لان هذا اختلاف فى الولاء مقصودا و ذلك يبتنى على بقاء الكتابة وانتقاضها فانها اذا فسخت مات عبدا واستقر الولاء على موالى الام واذا بقيت واتصل بها الاداء مات حرا وانتقل الولاء الى موالى الاب وهذا فصل مجتهد فيه فينقذ ما يلاقيه من القضاء فلهذا كان تعجيزا

مستعقر ہوگی ۔ اور یہ صورت چونکہ مجتہد فیہ ہے اس لئے جو قضاء اس سے ملاقی ہو وہ نافذ ہو جائے گی اس لئے یہ قضاء اس کے عاجز ہونے کا حکم ہے۔ تشریح قوله فان مات ... الخ ایک مکاتب آزاد عورت سے ایک بیٹا اور اور قاضی اس بچہ کی ولاء موالی ام کو دلوا دے تو اس سے مکاتب کا عاجز ہونا ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ اختلاف بالقصد ولاء میں واقع ہوا ہے جو کتابت کی بقاء اور اس کے انقاض پر مبنی ہے اس لئے کہ کتابت اگر فسخ ہو تو مکاتب مذکور غلامی میں مرے گا اور فرزند کی ولاء موالی ام پر مستقر ہوگی اور اگر کتابت باقی رہے اور بدل کتابت ادا ہو جائے تو وہ آزاد ہو کر مرے گا اور ولاء مولا اب کی طرف منتقل ہوگی اور یہ فصل چونکہ مجتہد فیہ ہے۔ چنانچہ پہلے گزر چکا کہ حضرت زید بن ثابت کے نزدیک موت مکاتب ہے کتابت فتح ہو جاتی ہے۔ اور بعض صحابہ کے نزدیک کتابت فسخ نہیں ہوتی۔ اس لئے قاضی کا موالی ام کے حق میں ولاء کا فیصلہ کرنا مجتہد فی فصل میں فیصلہ ہوالہذا بالا جماع نافذ ہو جائے گا اس لئے قاضی کا یہ حکم اس مکاتب کے عاجز ہو جانے کا حکم ہوا۔
If a mukatab dies and he has a son from a free woman and leaves a debt that fulfills his kitabah, then the son commits a crime, and the qadi gives judgment for it against the 'aqila of the mother, that is not a judgment of 'ajz of the mukatab, because this judgment confirms the ruling of the kitabah, since from its requirements is to attach the son to the masters of the mother and to obligate the 'aql upon them, but in a manner that has the possibility that he becomes free and then drags the wala to the masters of the father. And a judgment that confirms its ruling is not a declaration of 'ajz. And if the masters of the mother and the masters of the father dispute about his wala, and the qadi gives judgment for the masters of the mother, that is a judgment of 'ajz, because this is a dispute about wala intentionally, and that is based on the continuation or dissolution of the kitabah. If it is dissolved, he dies as a slave and the wala settles on the masters of the mother. If it continues and the payment is made, he dies free and the wala transfers to the masters of the father. This is a matter of ijtihad, so whatever judgment is given will be enforced. Therefore, this is a judgment of 'ajz. Translation in Urdu: If a mukatab died having a son from a free woman and left such debts that can fulfill his kitabah, then the son committed a crime, and the qadi ruled for its compensation upon the 'aqila of the mother, then this ruling does not prove that he declared the mukatab unable, because the requirement of the kitabah was to attach the boy to the mother's masters so that when the father pays the kitabah, he becomes attached to the father. Thus the qadi's ruling confirmed this requirement. But if the boy dies and the masters of the mother and father dispute about his wala, and the qadi rules in favor of the mother's masters, then that establishes the mukatab's 'ajz, because this dispute about wala is based on the survival or dissolution of the kitabah. If the kitabah is dissolved, the mukatab dies a slave and the son's wala settles on the mother's masters. If the kitabah remains and the kitabah price is paid, he dies free and the wala transfers to the father's masters. And this matter is a matter of ijtihad, so the qadi's ruling in favor of the mother's masters is enforced. Hence this judgment is a judgment of 'ajz of the mukatab.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage from the Kitab al-Mukatab discusses two scenarios regarding the effect of a qadi's judgment on the determination of a mukatab's 'ajz (inability to pay the kitabah). The first scenario: a mukatab dies, leaving a son from a free woman and sufficient debts to pay the kitabah. The son then commits a crime (jinayat), and the qadi rules that the mother's 'aqila (paternal blood-money paying relatives) must pay the blood money. This ruling does NOT constitute a declaration of the mukatab's 'ajz. Why? Because this ruling actually confirms the kitabah's requirements: it attaches the son's wala (patronage) temporarily to the mother's masters, with the possibility that if the father's kitabah is later paid, the wala transfers to the father's masters. A judgment that confirms the kitabah is not a judgment of 'ajz. The second scenario: if there is a direct dispute between the mother's masters and the father's masters over the son's wala, and the qadi rules in favor of the mother's masters, THEN that is a judgment of 'ajz. Why? Because the dispute about wala fundamentally depends on whether the kitabah is still valid or dissolved. If the kitabah is dissolved (meaning the mukatab died a slave), the wala goes to the mother's masters. If the kitabah remains and payment is made, the wala goes to the father's masters. By ruling for the mother's masters, the qadi has effectively decided that the kitabah is dissolved, meaning the mukatab died a slave, which implies he was 'ajiz. The author notes that this is a matter of ijtihad, referring to the Companion Zayd ibn Thabit's view that the death of a mukatab dissolves the kitabah, while other Companions disagreed. Therefore, the qadi's judgment is enforced (nāfidh). This passage illustrates a nuanced Hanafi position: not all qadi rulings that involve the mukatab's family imply 'ajz; only those that directly decide the wala issue do.

Key Terms
المكاتب (al-mukatab): A slave who enters a contract of kitabah with his master to pay a specified sum for his freedom.
العجز (al-'ajz): Inability of the mukatab to pay the kitabah price, leading to annulment of the contract and return to slavery.
الولاء (al-wala): The patronage/clientage relationship established after manumission, determining inheritance rights.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first scenario, why does the qadi's ruling on the son's 'aqila not constitute a judgment of 'ajz for the mukatab?
A) Because the qadi intended to favor the father's masters.
B) Because it confirms the kitabah by attaching the son to the mother's masters with possibility of later transfer.
C) Because the son is minor.
D) Because the debt was insufficient.

Key Takeaway
Only a qadi's ruling that directly decides the wala of the mukatab's son constitutes a judgment of 'ajz; a ruling on the son's 'aqila does not.

Mukatab's Sadaqat to Master: Change of Ownership Makes It Halal
Ruling and proof for sadaqat paid by mukatab to master

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of tabaddul al-mulk to explain why sadaqat given by a mukatab to his master becomes halal upon 'ajz, and distinguish this from the case of the rich or Hashimi.

Core Idea
Sadaqat paid to the master becomes halal because ownership changes: from sadaqah to compensation for emancipation.

In this passage, al-Hidayah addresses a specific scenario: a mukatab (slave under contract of emancipation) gives some of the sadaqat he receives (e.g., zakat) to his master, and later becomes unable to pay the remaining kitabah (becomes 'ajiz). The question is whether that payment is lawful (halal) for the master. The Hanafi ruling, supported by the hadith of Barirah, states that it is halal because the ownership of the property has changed: the mukatab owned it as sadaqah, and the master receives it as compensation for the emancipation, not as sadaqah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Condition
First, extract the explicit ruling: the sadaqat paid by the mukatab to his master, followed by his 'ajz, is halal (pure and lawful) for the master. Note the condition: the payment must have been made before 'ajz.
This is the core ruling of the passage.
2
Locate the Proof (Dalil)
The proof is the hadith of Barirah (radiallahu anha): the Prophet said about the meat given in charity to her, 'It is sadaqah for her, and for us a gift.' This shows that what was sadaqah for the slave becomes a gift (or compensation) for the owner, indicating a change in ownership.
The hadith is quoted in the passage: 'هى لها صدقة ولنا هدية'.
3
Understand the Principle (Tabaddul al-Mulk)
The key legal principle is 'change of ownership' (tabaddul al-mulk). The mukatab owned the sadaqah as a recipient. By paying it as kitabah, the master receives it as compensation for emancipation, not as sadaqah. Therefore, the prohibition on the master taking sadaqah does not apply.
This is why it becomes halal despite the master being generally forbidden from receiving sadaqah.
4
Distinguish from the Case of the Rich or Hashimi
If a rich person or a Hashimi (descendant of the Prophet) is simply permitted to use sadaqah that belongs to someone else, it does not become halal because ownership has not changed. The rich/Hashimi consumes it on the original owner's ownership, so the same restriction applies. The passage contrasts this using an analogy of a fasid purchase.
This distinction highlights the importance of ownership transfer.
5
Note the Intra-Hanafi Nuance
Imam Muhammad holds that 'ajz itself causes the change in ownership. Imam Abu Yusuf holds that 'ajz merely confirms the master's ownership that was already established from the contract. However, both agree on the halal status of the sadaqah for the master.
The difference is theoretical; the practical ruling is the same.

He said: Whatever a mukatab pays from sadaqat to his master and then becomes 'ajiz, that is good/halal for the master due to change of ownership. Because the slave takes possession of it as sadaqah, and the master takes it as compensation for the emancipation, and the prophetic indication in the hadith of Barirah points to that: 'It is sadaqah for her, and for us a gift.' This is contrary to permitting it for the rich and the Hashimi, because the one for whom it is permitted takes it on the ownership of the one who permits it, so the ownership does not change, so it is not good for him. Its analogue is the buyer in a fasid purchase, if he permits it to someone else, it is not good for him; if he makes him owner, it becomes good. And if he becomes 'ajiz before paying to the master, the answer is also like this. This is apparent according to Muhammad because ownership changes by 'ajz according to him, and likewise according to Abu Yusuf, although by 'ajz the master's ownership is confirmed according to him, because there is no impurity in the sadaqah itself; the impurity is in the act of taking due to it being humiliating for him. So it is not permissible for the rich without need, and for the Hashimi due to additional honor. The taking did not occur from the master, so he becomes like the wayfarer when he reaches his home, and the poor person when he becomes wealthy, while what they took from sadaqah remains in their hands, where it becomes good for them. Upon this, if the mukatab becomes free and becomes wealthy, what remains of sadaqah in his hand becomes good for him. Translation in Urdu: Whatever a mukatab paid from sadaqat to his master, then became 'ajiz, that wealth is halal for the master due to change of ownership. Because the slave took possession of it as sadaqah and the master took it as a substitute for emancipation. The prophetic indication in the hadith of Barirah is that it is sadaqah for her and for us a gift. This is contrary to when it is permitted for a rich or Hashimi person. Because the one for whom it is permitted consumes it on the ownership of the permitter, so ownership does not change, so it is not halal. But if he makes him owner, it becomes halal. And if he becomes 'ajiz before giving to the master, the answer is also this. And this is apparent according to Imam Muhammad because 'ajz changes ownership according to him, and likewise according to Abu Yusuf, although 'ajz confirms the master's ownership according to him, because there is no filth in the sadaqah itself; the filth is in the act of taking due to it being humiliating. So it is not permissible for the rich without need, and for the Hashimi due to additional honor. The taking did not occur from the master, so he becomes like the wayfarer when he reaches his home, and the poor person when he becomes wealthy, while what they took from sadaqah remains in their hands, where it is halal for them. And upon this, if the mukatab is freed and becomes wealthy, what remains of sadaqah in his hand becomes halal for him.

Commentary
This passage from the Kitab al-Mukatab presents a ruling and its proof regarding sadaqat (charity) given by a mukatab to his master. The ruling: if a mukatab pays sadaqat (e.g., from the zakat funds he receives) to his master, and then later becomes 'ajiz (unable to pay the kitabah), that wealth is halal (pure and lawful) for the master. The reason is that there is a change in ownership (tabaddul al-mulk): the slave (mukatab) possessed the sadaqah as a recipient, and when he pays it to his master, the master takes it as compensation (iwad) for the eventual emancipation — i.e., as payment towards the kitabah. The proof is the hadith of Barirah (radiallahu anha), where the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) said: 'It (the meat given in charity) is sadaqah for her (Barirah), but for us it is a gift.' This indicates that what was sadaqah for the slave becomes a gift for the master, meaning ownership changes. The passage then contrasts this with a rich or Hashimi (descendant of the Prophet) person being permitted to consume something that was originally sadaqah for someone else — it is not halal for them because there is no change in ownership; they are taking it on the ownership of the original owner. The analogy (nazir) is: if someone buys something in a fasid (defective) sale and then permits another to use it, it does not become halal for that other because ownership hasn't transferred. But if he gives ownership, it becomes halal. Similarly, if a mukatab becomes 'ajiz before paying the sadaqah to the master, the same answer applies. The passage then notes that Imam Muhammad's view is clear because according to him, 'ajz (inability) changes ownership (the master's ownership is established from the time of kitabah but confirmed at 'ajz). Imam Abu Yusuf also agrees, though he holds that 'ajz merely confirms the master's ownership; but since the impurity (khubth) is not in the sadaqah itself but in the act of taking it when it's humiliating (idhlal), and since the master did not take it as a humiliating act (he took it as payment for emancipation), it is halal. This is similar to a wayfarer (ibn al-sabil) who receives sadaqah and then reaches his home (i.e., becomes able) — what remains in his hand is halal for him. Also, a poor person who receives sadaqah then becomes wealthy — what remains is halal. The same applies to a mukatab who is freed and becomes wealthy: the remaining sadaqah in his hand becomes halal for him.

Key Terms
الصدقات (al-sadaqat): Voluntary or obligatory charity given to eligible recipients; here specifically referring to what a mukatab receives as sadaqah.
تبدل الملك (tabaddul al-mulk): Change in ownership; in this context, the sadaqah becomes owned by the master as compensation for emancipation.
المولى (al-mawla): The master of the mukatab (the owner of the slave).
العجز (al-'ajz): Inability of the mukatab to pay the remaining installments of the kitabah, triggering the rescission of the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary basis for the sadaqat paid by a mukatab to his master becoming halal after the mukatab's 'ajz?
A) The master's need for the money.
B) The hadith of Barirah, indicating a change of ownership.
C) The mukatab's consent to give it as a gift.
D) The fact that 'ajz makes the master the owner of all the mukatab's property.

Key Takeaway
When a mukatab pays sadaqat to his master and then becomes 'ajiz, the payment becomes halal for the master because ownership changes from sadaqah to compensation for emancipation.

8 min
Master's Option When Mukatab Becomes Incapable After Crime
Explains ruling and intra-Hanafi dispute on slave's crime after kitaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the master's option when a mukatab commits a crime and becomes incapable before adjudication, and evaluate Zufr's counter-argument.

Core Idea
Kitaba is a removable preventer; the master's option remains until adjudication transfers the right to value.

This lesson deals with a specific intra-Hanafi dispute about the status of a crime committed by a mukatab (a slave under contract of gradual manumission) who subsequently becomes incapable of fulfilling the kitaba. The core issue is whether the obligation immediately becomes a debt (as Zufr argues) or remains tied to the person, giving the master a choice to surrender or pay ransom (as Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold). The passage uses analogical reasoning (qiyas) with an absconding slave and distinguishes kitaba from irrevocable contracts like tadbir and istilad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario and the variable
The scenario: a slave commits a crime, then his master makes him a mukatab without knowing of the crime, then the slave becomes incapable (ajz). The variable is whether the crime was adjudicated before the ajz.
2
State the Hanafi position for each sub-case
If ajz occurs before any adjudication: master has option to surrender slave or pay fidyah. If adjudication occurred during kitaba, then ajz converts the obligation into a debt for which the slave is sold. This is the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf retracted to it.
This is the mufta bihi view.
3
Present Zufr's counter-argument
Zufr holds that even before adjudication, if the slave becomes incapable, the obligation becomes a debt immediately. His proof: the preventer (kitaba) existed at the time of the crime, so the crime must necessitate value, just like with a mudabbar or umm walad.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: kitaba is removable (the slave might pay and free himself, or fail and revert to slavery), so the preventer is unstable. Hence, the right does not transfer to value immediately; it depends on adjudication or consent. This is analogous to a sold slave who absconds before delivery: rescission depends on a judge's ruling due to fluctuation.
Tadbir and istilad are distinguished because they are irrevocable.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Under Zufr's view, before adjudication the slave would be sold immediately for the value. Under the Hanafi view, the master retains the option to choose surrender or ransom until adjudication transfers the right to value.

قوله وصار کا لعبد المبيع ... الخ - مكاتب مذکور کا حکم ایسا ہو گیا جیسے فروخت شدہ غلام قبصہ سے پہلے بھاگ جائے کہ بیع کا انفساخ حکم قاضی پر موقوف رہتا ہے کیونکہ اس کی واپسی کے احتمال سے تردد ہے۔ ایسے ہی یہاں ہوگا بخلاف تدبیر و استیلا د کے کہ یہ کسی حال میں بھی قابل زوال نہیں ہیں۔ فكان الموجب في الابداء هو القيمة
And when the slave commits a crime, then his master makes him a mukatab without knowing of the crime, then he becomes incapable, he surrenders or ransoms, because this is the original obligation of the slave's crime, and he was not aware of the crime at the time of kitaba to become chooser of ransom, except that kitaba prevents surrender, so when it is removed the original ruling returns. Similarly, when a mukatab commits a crime and it is not adjudicated until he becomes incapable, due to what we said of removal of the preventer. But if it is adjudicated against him during his kitaba, then he becomes incapable, it is a debt for which he is sold, because the right transfers from the person to its value by adjudication. This is the saying of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf returned to it. He used to say first that he is sold for it even if he becomes incapable before adjudication, and this is the saying of Zufr, because the preventer from surrender, i.e., kitaba, existed at the time of the crime, so as it occurred it necessitated the value, like in the crime of a mudabbar or umm walad. Our proof: the preventer is subject to removal due to fluctuation, and transfer does not take effect immediately, so it depends on adjudication or consent, and it is like a sold slave who absconds before delivery: rescission depends on adjudication due to fluctuation and possibility of return. This is unlike tadbir and istilad, for they are not subject to removal in any case.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the ruling when a slave commits a crime, then his master makes him a mukatab without knowing of the crime, and then the slave becomes incapable of fulfilling the kitaba (ajz). The text states the ruling: the master has the option to either surrender the slave to the victim or pay the fidyah (ransom). This is because the original obligation of the slave's crime is that the master surrenders him, but kitaba prevented that, and once the kitaba ends due to ajz, the original ruling returns. Similarly, if a mukatab commits a crime and becomes incapable before any adjudication, the same applies. However, if the crime was adjudicated during the kitaba and then the slave becomes incapable, the obligation becomes a debt against the slave, and he is sold to pay it. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold this view, and Abu Yusuf retracted his earlier opinion to agree. Zufr holds that even before adjudication, if the slave becomes incapable, the obligation immediately becomes a debt (a value owed) because the preventer (kitaba) existed at the time of the crime, akin to a mudabbar or umm walad. The Hanafi response (based on Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that the preventer is removable due to the fluctuation of the slave's status (he might pay and become free or fail and become a slave), so the transfer to value does not happen immediately and depends on adjudication or consent. This is analogized to a sold slave who absconds before delivery: the contract rescission depends on a judge's ruling due to the possibility of the slave's return. The commentary emphasizes that tadbir and istilad are different because they are irrevocable.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract of kitaba with his master to purchase his freedom by paying installments.
كتابة (kitaba): The contract between master and slave for gradual manumission upon payment.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave whose manumission is deferred until after the master's death.
عجز (ajz): Incapacity of the mukatab to fulfill the kitaba payment, leading to reversion to slavery.
فدية (fidyah): Ransom paid by the master to the victim in lieu of surrendering the slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, if a slave commits a crime, is made a mukatab without the master knowing, and then becomes incapable (ajz) before any adjudication, what is the master's option?
A) He must surrender the slave.
B) He must pay the fidyah.
C) He may choose to either surrender the slave or pay fidyah.
D) The slave is immediately sold for the debt.

Key Takeaway
The master's option remains until a qadi's ruling transfers the crime's obligation from the slave's person to its value.

Ruling on Mukatab Who Commits Crime and Becomes Unable to Pay
Explains the effect of incapacity after a crime on the mukatab's kitabah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on a mukatab who commits a crime and later becomes unable to pay, and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the timing of his sale.

Core Idea
The mukatab's kitabah creates uncertainty, so his sale for a crime depends on a judge's ruling or mutual agreement.

In this passage, Marghinani discusses a nuanced case: a mukatab (slave under contract of manumission) commits a crime, then becomes unable to continue paying his kitabah. The key question is whether the master can immediately hand him over or sell him to compensate the victim. The Hanafi school holds that the answer depends on whether a judgment has been passed, but there is an intra-madhhab difference with Abu Yusuf and Zufar.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
Identify the facts: the mukatab commits a crime and later becomes unable to pay the kitabah. The ruling depends on whether a judgment for the crime has already been passed.
The case assumes the mukatab's incapacity occurs after the crime, not before.
2
Identify the relied-upon position
The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that of the two (Abu Yusuf in his final view and Muhammad al-Shaybani): if no judgment, the master may hand over the mukatab; if judgment passed, he must be sold.
This is the position of the Sahibayn.
3
Examine the opposing views
Abu Yusuf's first view: the mukatab is sold even without a judgment. Zufar: the crime becomes property immediately, so the right transfers at once.
These views are considered less authoritative.
4
Analyze the Hanafi proof
The proof is based on taraddud (uncertainty): the kitabah is not permanent (like tadbir or istilad), so the right to the slave's person does not transfer to his value until judgment or agreement removes the uncertainty. A qiyas is made to a sold slave who runs away before possession.
The key distinction is that kitabah is subject to dissolution, unlike tadbir.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: under the relied-upon view, the master cannot sell without a judgment; under Abu Yusuf's first view, he could. This affects the rights of the victim and the mukatab.
The tarjih is in favor of the Sahibayn.

قوله وصار کا لعبد المبيع ... الخ - مكاتب مذکور کا حکم ایسا ہو گیا جیسے فروخت شدہ غلام قبصہ سے پہلے بھاگ جائے کہ بیع کا انفساخ حکم قاضی پر موقوف رہتا ہے کیونکہ اس کی واپسی کے احتمال سے تردد ہے۔ ایسے ہی یہاں ہوگا بخلاف تدبیر و استیلا د کے کہ یہ کسی حال میں بھی قابل زوال نہیں ہیں۔ فكان الموجب في الابداء هو القيمة
He will not become one who chooses ransom by doing this. It is just that the master's making him a mukatab prevents giving the slave. When this impediment is removed, the original ruling returns. He said: Likewise, if the mukatab commits a crime and the ruling for the crime has not yet been made that he becomes unable to pay the kitabah, then the same ruling applies: the master has the option to hand over this slave because what prevented giving has disappeared. He said: And if judgment was passed against this mukatab to pay compensation, then he becomes unable to pay the kitabah, now that compensation becomes a debt on him and he will be sold for it, because due to the judge's ruling the right of crime has transferred from his person to his value. This is the view of the two (Sahibayn) and also the final view of Imam Abu Yusuf. Abu Yusuf's first view is that he will be sold for this right even if his inability occurred before the judge's ruling. He said: Our proof is that what is an impediment (i.e., kitabah) is subject to dissolution due to uncertainty. That is, there is doubt: perhaps he will pay and become free, or become unable and remain a slave (so the kitabah will be removed). Thus, currently the mentioned right has not transferred from his person to his value. So it remains pending on the judge's ruling or mutual agreement. The conclusion is that the mukatab's crime is not property in our view, except through judgment, mutual consent, or by leaving an estate sufficient for the kitabah after death. And from Zufar: it becomes property immediately. He said: And it becomes like a sold slave who runs away before possession: the rescission of the sale remains pending on the judge's ruling because of the doubt of his return. Similarly here, unlike tadbir and istilad which are not subject to dissolution in any case. So the obligating factor for handing over is the value.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a mukatab who commits a crime and then becomes unable to pay the kitabah. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): if no judgment has been passed for the crime, the master may hand over the mukatab to the victim because the impediment of kitabah is removed. But if judgment has been passed, the right to the crime is transferred from the slave's person to his value, so he is sold to satisfy the debt. Imam Abu Yusuf initially held that the slave is sold even without judgment, but he retracted. Zufar held that the crime becomes property immediately. The Hanafi proof is based on the concept of taraddud (uncertainty): the kitabah is not permanent like tadbir or istilad, so the right remains pending until judgment or agreement.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has a contract (kitabah) with his master to earn his freedom by paying installments.
کتابت (kitabah): The contract of manumission by payment, involving a specified sum paid in installments.
تردد (taraddud): A state of uncertainty; here meaning that the kitabah is subject to being either fulfilled or rescinded.
تاديب (tadbir): A declaration by a master that a slave will be free upon the master's death.
استيلاد (istilad): A female slave who bears a child to her master, becoming umm walad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Immediately after he commits the crime
B) Only after a judge passes a ruling for compensation
C) Only after he becomes unable to pay the kitabah
D) Never, because the kitabah protects him

Key Takeaway
The mukatab's sale for a crime is contingent on a judgment due to the taraddud of kitabah; without judgment, the master may only hand him over.

Effect of Master's Death on the Kitabah Contract
Explains that the kitabah remains valid after the master's death and payment is made to heirs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the effect of the master's death on the kitabah contract and explain why a single heir cannot free the mukatab individually.

Core Idea
The kitabah contract survives the master's death; only collective freeing by all heirs is valid.

In this lesson, we examine what happens when the master of a mukatab (a slave under a kitabah contract) passes away. The Hanafi school holds that the kitabah is not rescinded—the contract continues and the mukatab must pay the installments to the master's heirs. We will explore the rational proof for this ruling and the important consequences regarding who can manumit the mukatab and how.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its rationale
First, note the core ruling: the kitabah is not rescinded by the master's death. The reason given is that voiding it would destroy the mukatab's right to freedom, and a right is not voided by death. The text draws an analogy to an ordinary debt: if a creditor dies, the debt remains payable to heirs. Similarly, the kitabah debt remains.
2
Understand the payment destination
Determine where the mukatab must now pay: to the master's heirs, in the same installments as before. The heirs are successors (khalifah) in collection, but the contract itself does not change.
This is true only if the master was healthy at the time of the kitabah; if he was ill, different rules apply.
3
Examine the rule on manumission by heirs
Analyze the scenario where one heir attempts to free the mukatab. The ruling is that it is ineffective because a single heir does not own the mukatab individually. The mukatab is not owned by inheritance like ordinary property.
4
Apply the collective manumission rule
Now consider when all heirs jointly free the mukatab. That is effective, and the kitabah payment is dropped as an ibra' (absolution) from all heirs.
The freeing is treated as an absolution from the debt of kitabah, which is the right of the heirs.
5
Connect to the underlying principle
Step back and see the principle: rights are not extinguished by death, and the kitabah is a right of the mukatab. The contract is a cause of freedom, and a person's cause of right is his right. This is a rational (aqli) proof by analogy to debts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مکاتب کا آقا فوت ہو جائے تو کتابت فسخ نہیں ہوگی تا کہ مکاتب کے حق کا ابطال لازم نہ آئے

تشریح قوله واذا امات ... الخ - اگر مکاتب کا آقا مر جائے تو کتابت فسخ نہ ہوگی ۔ تا کہ اس کا نتیجہ یہ نہ ہو کہ مکاتب کا حق مٹ جائے ۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ کتابت آزادی کا سبب ہے اور آزادی مکاتب کا حق ہے اور کسی شخص کے حق کا جو سبب ہو وہ بھی اس کا حق ہو جاتا ہے پس کتابت اس کا حق ہوا۔ اور موت کی وجہ سے حق باطل نہیں ہوتا جیسے کسی کا دوسرے کے ذمہ قرض ہوا اور صاحب قرض مرجائے تو قرض
باطل نہیں ہو جاتا۔ قوله وقيل له الخ - اب مکاتب مذکور سے کہا جائے گا کہ آقا کے ورثہ کو بدل کتابت مقسطون کے مطابق ادا کر اس لئے کہ وہ آزادی کا مستحق اسی طور پر ہوا تھا او اسی طریقہ پر سبب منعقد ہوا تھا تو وہ اس صفت پر باقی رہے گا اور اس میں کوئی تغیر نہ ہوگا۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ آقا جب صحیح و تندرست ہو تو اس کا کل بدل کتابت کو مؤ جل کرنے کا تصرف صحیح ہوتا ہے جیسے کل بدل کتابت ساقط کرنے کا تصرف صحیح ہے اور یہاں مسئلہ کی وضع چونکہ علی الاطلاق ہے اس سے معلوم ہو گیا کہ آقا صحیح تندرست تھا لہذا اس کا تصرف صحیح ہوا بخلاف اس کے جب آقا مریض ہو اور وہ غلام کو مکاتب کرے کہ اس صورت میں مکاتب یا تو فی الحال اپنی دو تہائی قیمت ادا کرے گا یا اس کو رقیق کر دیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ مریض ہونے کی صورت میں آقا کا تصرف تاجیل واسقاط تہائی کے علاوہ میں صحیح نہیں ہوتا۔ قوله الا ان الورثه الخ -قول سابق ولا يتغیر “ سے استثناء ہے اور گو ایک سوال کا جواب ہے ۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ سبب حریت کیسے متغیر نہ ہو گا جب کہ آقا کا حق استیفاء بدل تھا جو ورثہ کے لئے ہو گیا اور یہی تغیر ہے۔
جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ آقا کے ورثہ صرف مال کتابت وصول کرنے میں اس کے خلیفہ ہوں گے اور صرف اتنی بات سے نہ حق متغیر ہوتا ہے نہ عقد کتابت ( لانها باقية كما كانت ) جیسے ایک شخص کا کسی کے ذمہ قرض ہو اور صاحب قرض مرجائے تو وصولیابی میں اس کے ورثہ اس کے قائم مقام ہوتے ہیں اور مقروض جیسے مورث کو اڑا کرنے سے بری ہو جاتا ہے ایسے ہی ورثہ کو ادا کرنے سے بری ہو جاتا ہے پس جیسے
دیگر تمام دیون میں ورثہ اس کے خلیفہ ہوتے ہیں اور اس کو تغیر نہیں کہا جاتا ایسے ہی دین کتابت میں بھی خلافت کو تغیر نہیں کہا جائیگا۔ قوله فان اعتقه احد الورثة ... الخ - پھر گر آقا کے ورثہ میں سے کسی وارث نے مکاتب مذکور کو آزاد کر دیا تو اس کا آزاد کرنا
If the master of the mukatab dies, the kitabah is not rescinded, so that the right of the mukatab is not voided. He said: And when the master of the mukatab dies, the kitabah is not rescinded, lest it lead to voiding the right of the mukatab, because the kitabah is a cause of freedom, and a person's cause of right is his right. And it will be said to him: 'Pay the money to the master's heirs according to your installments,' because he became entitled to freedom in this way, and the cause was contracted thus, so it remains in this condition and does not change, except that the heirs succeed him in collecting. Then if one of the heirs frees him, his freeing is not effective because he does not own him. And this is because the mukatab is not owned by other means of ownership, so likewise not by inheritance. But if all free him, he becomes free and the kitabah payment is dropped from him, because it becomes an absolution from the kitabah, for it is their right and inheritance has occurred in it. So when the mukatab is freed from the kitabah, he becomes free, as if the master had absolved him. However, if one heir frees him, it does not become an absolution for his share, because we would establish an absolution by implication to validate his freeing, but freeing is not established by absolution of some or payment in the mukatab, neither in part nor in whole. And there is no way to consider it an absolution of the whole due to the right of the remaining heirs. And Allah knows best. Translation: If the master of the mukatab dies, the kitabah is not rescinded, so that this does not lead to voiding the right of the mukatab, because the kitabah is a cause of freedom, and a person's cause of right is his right. And the mukatab will be told to pay the wealth to the master's heirs according to his installments, because he became entitled to freedom in this way, and the cause was contracted thus, so it will remain in this condition, unchanged, except that the heirs become his successors in collection. Then if any heir frees him, his freeing is not effective, because he is not the owner. And the reason is that the mukatab is not owned by other means of ownership, so likewise not by inheritance. Yes, if all the heirs free him, he becomes free and the kitabah payment drops from him, because this would be an absolution from the kitabah, since the payment is their right and inheritance has occurred in it. So when he is absolved from the kitabah, he becomes free, just as if the master had absolved him. But if one heir freed him, this would not be an absolution for his share, because we would establish an absolution by way of implication to make his freeing valid, but freeing is not established by absolution of some or payment in the mukatab, neither in his entirety nor in part. And there is no way to consider it an absolution of the whole due to the right of the remaining heirs. And Allah knows best. Commentary: He said: And if he dies... The explanation: If the master of the mukatab dies, the kitabah will not be rescinded, so that the result is not that the mukatab's right is obliterated. The reason is that the kitabah is a cause of freedom, and freedom is the right of the mukatab, and the cause of a person's right becomes his right. So the kitabah became his right. And a right is not voided by death, just as if someone has a debt owed to him and the creditor dies, the debt does not become void. He said: And it will be said to him... Now this mukatab will be told to pay the kitabah to the master's heirs according to the installments, because he became entitled to freedom in this way, and the cause was contracted in this manner, so it remains in this condition and no change occurs. The reason is that when the master is healthy, his act of deferring the entire kitabah is valid, just as his act of remitting the entire kitabah is valid. And since the situation here is absolute, it is understood that the master was healthy, so his act was valid. Unlike when the master is ill and he makes the slave a mukatab: in that case, the mukatab must either pay two-thirds of his value immediately or be returned to slavery, because in the case of illness, the master's act of deferral and remission beyond one-third is not valid. He said: Except that the heirs... This is an exception to the previous statement 'and does not change,' and it is the answer to a question. The question is: How does the cause of freedom not change when the master's right to collect the payment has become for the heirs, and this is a change? The gist of the answer is that the master's heirs are only his successors in collecting the kitabah money, and from this alone neither the right nor the contract of kitabah changes (because it remains as it was), just as when a person has a debt owed to him and the creditor dies, his heirs stand in his place for collection, and the debtor is discharged by paying the heirs just as he would have been discharged by paying the original creditor. So just as in all other debts, the heirs are successors and this is not considered a change, similarly in the debt of kitabah, succession is not called a change. He said: Then if one of the heirs frees him... Then if one of the master's heirs frees this mukatab, his freeing is not effective.
Source pages p. 199

Commentary
This passage explains the effect of the master's death on the kitabah contract. The ruling is that the contract remains valid and is not rescinded, to protect the mukatab's right to freedom. The mukatab must continue paying the installments to the master's heirs. The heirs merely succeed the master in collecting the debt; the contract itself does not change. If a single heir tries to free the mukatab, it is ineffective because that heir does not own the mukatab individually (the mukatab is not owned by inheritance as normal property). However, if all the heirs collectively free him, the freeing is effective and the kitabah payment is dropped, treated as an absolution from their right. The text also distinguishes the case where the master was ill at the time of the kitabah: if ill, the mukatab must pay two-thirds of his value immediately or be returned to slavery, because a sick person's actions beyond one-third of his estate are limited. This ruling is based on the principle that rights are not voided by death and that the kitabah is a personal right of the mukatab.

Key Terms
کتابت (kitabah): The contract of manumission by payment; here it remains valid after the master's death.
ابراء (ibra'): Absolution or release from a debt; here, the heirs' collective freeing is considered an ibra' from the kitabah payment.
خلیفہ (khalifah): Successor; the heirs are successors of the master in collecting the kitabah money.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi fiqh, what is the effect if one heir of the deceased master frees the mukatab?
A) The mukatab becomes free and the kitabah payment is reduced by the heir's share.
B) The freeing is invalid because one heir does not own the mukatab individually.
C) The mukatab becomes free but still owes the other heirs their shares.
D) The freeing is valid only if the heir pays the other heirs their shares.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the kitabah contract survives the master's death; the mukatab continues paying the heirs, and only the collective manumission by all heirs is valid, treating it as an absolution from the debt.

intermediate
8 min
Effect of Master's Death on the Kitabah Contract
Explains survival of kitabah after master's death and payment to heirs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the kitabah contract remains valid after the master's death and explain the obligation of the mukatab to pay installments to the heirs.

Core Idea
Master's death does not void kitabah; heirs collect installments just as a creditor's heirs collect a debt.

When a master who contracted kitabah with his slave dies, one might think the contract ends. The Hanafi school clarifies that the contract remains intact. The mukatab's right to freedom continues, and the heirs simply take over collection of the payment installments. This ruling is based on the analogy to ordinary debts, which are not extinguished by the creditor's death.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
State that the kitabah contract is not rescinded upon the master's death. The text explicitly says 'والكتابة لا تفسخ' (the kitabah is not voided).
This is the foundation; the remaining details build on it.
2
Understand the legal reasoning
Kitabah is a cause of freedom, and freedom is the mukatab's right. Once a right is established, death does not invalidate it, just like a debt right.
The analogy to debt (dayn) is key: if a creditor dies, the debtor still owes the heirs.
3
Apply the analogy to the mukatab's obligation
Therefore, the mukatab must continue paying the installments (badal al-kitabah) to the heirs, according to the same schedule agreed with the master.
This is because the contract was valid and the master was healthy when it was made.
4
Contrast with the sick master scenario
The text notes that if the master was terminally ill at the time of kitabah, the ruling differs: the mukatab must immediately pay two-thirds of his value or be re-enslaved.
This shows that the master's health affects the validity of deferring payment.
5
Note the limit of heir authority
Heirs are only successors in collection; they do not own the mukatab and cannot change the contract terms.
This prepares for the next lesson on manumission.

كتاب المكاتب

آزادی کا سبب ہے اور آدمی کے حق کا سبب بھی اسی کا حق ہوتا ہے اور مکاتب سے کہا جائے گا کہ آقا کے ورثہ کو مال ادا کر اپنی قسطوں کے مطابق کیونکہ وہ آزادی کا مستحق اسی طور پر ہوا تھا اور اسی طور پر سبب منعقد ہوا تھا تو اسی صفت پر باقی رہے گا متغیر نہ ہوگا بجز آنکہ ورثہ اس کے خلیفہ ہو جائیں گے وصول کرنے میں پھر اگر کسی وارث نے اس کو آزاد کر دیا تو اس کا آزاد کرنا نافذ نہ ہوگا کیونکہ وہ اس کا مالک نہیں ہے اور اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ مکاتب دیگر اسباب ملک سے مملوک نہیں ہوتا تو ایسے ہی وراثت کے سبب سے بھی نہ ہو گا ہاں اگر سب ورثہ آزاد کر دیں تو آزاد ہو جائے گا اور اس سے بدل کتابت ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ بدل کتابت سے بری کرنا ہوگا اس لئے کہ عوض ان کا حق ہے اور آئمیں وراثت جاری ہو چکی پس جب بر کا تب بدل کتابت سے بری ہو گیا تو آزاد ہو جائے گا جیسے اگر آقا اس کو بری کرتا لیکن اگر ایک وارث نے آزاد کیا تو یہ اس کے حصہ سے ابراء نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ہم تو اس کا عتق صحیح کرنے کے لئے بطریق اقتضاء ابراء ثابت کرتے ہیں اور بعض کے بری یا ادا کرنے سے مکاتب میں اعتاق ثابت نہیں ہوتا نہ اس کے کل میں نہ جزء میں اور کل کا ابراء قرار دینے کی کوئی درجہ نہیں باقی ورثہ کے حق کی وجہ سے۔ واللہ اعلم

تشریح قوله واذا امات ... الخ - اگر مکاتب کا آقا مر جائے تو کتابت فسخ نہ ہوگی ۔ تا کہ اس کا نتیجہ یہ نہ ہو کہ مکاتب کا حق مٹ جائے ۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ کتابت آزادی کا سبب ہے اور آزادی مکاتب کا حق ہے اور کسی شخص کے حق کا جو سبب ہو وہ بھی اس کا حق ہو جاتا ہے پس کتابت اس کا حق ہوا۔ اور موت کی وجہ سے حق باطل نہیں ہوتا جیسے کسی کا دوسرے کے ذمہ قرض ہوا اور صاحب قرض مرجائے تو قرض باطل نہیں ہو جاتا۔ قوله وقيل له الخ - اب مکاتب مذکور سے کہا جائے گا کہ آقا کے ورثہ کو بدل کتابت مقسطون کے مطابق ادا کر اس لئے کہ وہ آزادی کا مستحق اسی طور پر ہوا تھا او اسی طریقہ پر سبب منعقد ہوا تھا تو وہ اس صفت پر باقی رہے گا اور اس میں کوئی تغیر نہ ہوگا۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ آقا جب صحیح و تندرست ہو تو اس کا کل بدل کتابت کو مؤ جل کرنے کا تصرف صحیح ہوتا ہے جیسے کل بدل کتابت ساقط کرنے کا تصرف صحیح ہے اور یہاں مسئلہ کی وضع چونکہ علی الاطلاق ہے اس سے معلوم ہو گیا کہ آقا صحیح تندرست تھا لہذا اس کا تصرف صحیح ہوا بخلاف اس کے جب آقا مریض ہو اور وہ غلام کو مکاتب کرے کہ اس صورت میں مکاتب یا تو فی الحال اپنی دو تہائی قیمت ادا کرے گا یا اس کو رقیق کر دیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ مریض ہونے کی صورت میں آقا کا تصرف تاجیل واسقاط تہائی کے علاوہ میں صحیح نہیں ہوتا۔ قوله الا ان الورثه الخ -قول سابق ولا يتغیر “ سے استثناء ہے اور گو ایک سوال کا جواب ہے ۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ سبب حریت کیسے متغیر نہ ہو گا جب کہ آقا کا حق استیفاء بدل تھا جو ورثہ کے لئے ہو گیا اور یہی تغیر ہے۔
جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ آقا کے ورثہ صرف مال کتابت وصول کرنے میں اس کے خلیفہ ہوں گے اور صرف اتنی بات سے نہ حق متغیر ہوتا ہے نہ عقد کتابت ( لانها باقية كما كانت ) جیسے ایک شخص کا کسی کے ذمہ قرض ہو اور صاحب قرض مرجائے تو وصولیابی میں اس کے ورثہ اس کے قائم مقام ہوتے ہیں اور مقروض جیسے مورث کو اڑا کرنے سے بری ہو جاتا ہے ایسے ہی ورثہ کو ادا کرنے سے بری ہو جاتا ہے پس جیسے دیگر تمام دیون میں ورثہ اس کے خلیفہ ہوتے ہیں اور اس کو تغیر نہیں کہا جاتا ایسے ہی دین کتابت میں بھی خلافت کو تغیر نہیں کہا جائیگا۔ قوله فان اعتقه احد الورثة ... الخ - پھر گر آقا کے ورثہ میں سے کسی وارث نے مکاتب مذکور کو آزاد کر دیا تو اس کا آزاد کرنا نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ اس کا مالک نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ مکاتب اسباب ملک میں سے کسی سبب کے ذریعہ مملوک نہیں ہوتا۔ ولا عتق فيما لا یملکہ ابن آدم شرح اقطع میں ہے کہ امام شافعی کے ایک قول میں اس کا آزاد کرنا نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ لانه يصح عنده بيع المكاتب ويصح ان يملك آقا
قوله فان اعتقوه جميعاً ... الخ - اور اگر اس کو سب ورثہ نے آزاد کر دیا تو مقتضائے قیاس تو یہی ہے کہ اب بھی جائز نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ ان کا تصرف اس کی طرف مضاف ہوا ہے جو ان کی ملک نہیں ہے۔ لیکن استحسانا آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ اور اس کے ذمہ سے بدل کتابت ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ ان سب کا آزاد کرنا بدل کتابت سے بری کرنا ہے کیونکہ عوض مذکور ان کا حق ہے جس میں وراثت جاری ہو چکی تو ان کو اپنا حق چھوڑ دینے کا اختیار ہے۔ اور جب مکاتب عوض کتابت سے بری ہو گیا۔ تو وہ آزاد ہو جائے گا جیسے اگر خود اس کو بری کرتا تو وہ آزاد ہو جاتا۔ ممکن ہے کوئی یہ کہے کہ ایک کے آزاد کرنے سے بھی آزاد ہو جانا چاہیے کیونکہ ایک کا آزاد کرنا اپنے حصہ سے بری کرنا ہے۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ نہیں ہو سکتا۔ کیونکہ ہم نے جواعتقاق کو ابراہ قرار دیا ہے وہ تھے حق کے لئے بطریق اقتضاء کیا ہے اور بعض کے بری کرنے یا ادا کرنے سے مکاتب میں اعتاق ثابت نہیں ہوتا نہ اس کے جزء میں نہ کل میں۔
Book of the Mukatab. Freedom is a cause, and also a cause of a person's right is his right. The mukatab will be told: 'Pay the master's heirs according to your installments, because he became deserving of freedom in this manner and the cause was contracted in this manner, so it will remain in that state, unchanged, except that the heirs become his successors in collection. Then if one of the heirs manumits him, his manumission is not effective because he is not his owner, and the reason is that the mukatab is not owned through other causes of ownership, so likewise by inheritance it will not occur. Yes, if all heirs manumit him, he becomes free and the kitabah payment is dropped, because this is a discharge from the kitabah payment, since the consideration is their right and inheritance has taken effect. So when he is discharged from the kitabah payment, he becomes free, just as if the master had discharged him. But if one heir manumits him, this is not a discharge from his share, because we establish discharge by implication for the validity of his manumission, and manumission is not established in the mukatab by the discharge or payment of some, neither in whole nor in part, and there is no degree of making it a discharge of the whole due to the right of the remaining heirs. And Allah knows best. Explanation of his statement: 'And when the master dies...' etc. If the master of the mukatab dies, the kitabah is not rescinded, so that the mukatab's right is not eliminated. The reason is that kitabah is a cause of freedom, and freedom is the right of the mukatab, and whatever is a cause of a person's right also becomes his right. Thus kitabah became his right, and death does not invalidate a right, just as if someone has a debt on another and the creditor dies, the debt is not invalidated. His statement: 'And it will be said to him...' etc. Now the aforementioned mukatab will be told to pay the heirs the kitabah payment according to the installments, because he became deserving of freedom in this manner and the cause was contracted in this manner, so it will remain in that state and there will be no change. The reason is that when the master is healthy, his act of deferring the entire kitabah payment is valid, just as his act of dropping the entire kitabah payment is valid, and here the case is absolute, so it is known that the master was healthy, hence his act is valid, contrary to when the master is ill and he makes the slave a mukatab, in which case the mukatab will either pay two-thirds of his value immediately or he will be re-enslaved, because in the case of illness the master's act of deferral and dropping other than one-third is not valid. His statement: 'Except that the heirs...' etc. This is an exception from the previous statement 'and it does not change', and it is also an answer to a question. The question is: How does the cause of freedom not change when the master's right to receive the payment becomes for the heirs, and this is a change? The summary of the answer is that the master's heirs are only his successors in collecting the kitabah payment, and by this alone neither the right nor the contract of kitabah changes (because it remains as it was), just as if a person has a debt on someone and the creditor dies, in collection his heirs stand in his place, and the debtor is discharged by paying the heirs just as he would be discharged by paying the ancestor. So just as in all other debts the heirs are successors and this is not called a change, likewise in the debt of kitabah, the succession is not called a change. His statement: 'If one of the heirs manumits him...' etc. Then if one of the master's heirs manumits the aforementioned mukatab, his manumission is not effective because he is not his owner, since the mukatab is not owned through any cause of ownership. And there is no manumission in what a person does not own. In Sharh al-Aqta' it is stated that in one of Imam al-Shafi'i's opinions, his manumission would be effective because according to him the sale of the mukatab is valid and the master can own him. His statement: 'If they all manumit him...' etc. If all heirs manumit him, the logical requirement (qiyas) is that it is still not valid because their act pertains to someone not in their ownership. However, by istihsan, he becomes free and the kitabah payment is dropped from his liability. The reason for istihsan is that their collective manumission is a discharge from the kitabah payment because the said consideration is their right in which inheritance has taken effect, so they have the option to relinquish their right. And when the mukatab is discharged from the kitabah payment, he becomes free, just as if the master himself had discharged him. It is possible that someone might say that manumission by one should also free him because one's manumission is a discharge from his share. The answer is that this cannot be, because we have established manumission as a discharge by implication for the whole right, and manumission is not established in the mukatab by the discharge or payment of some, neither in part nor in whole.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage from Kitab al-Mukatab (Book of the Mukatab) in Ashraf ul-Hadaya explains the rulings concerning the contract of kitabah (deed of emancipation) when the master dies. The passage is structured as a commentary on the Hidayah, and it covers three main points: (1) the effect of the master's death on the kitabah contract, (2) the payment obligation of the mukatab to the heirs, and (3) the possibility of manumission by the heirs. The author begins by stating that the kitabah contract remains valid after the master's death; it is not rescinded. This is because kitabah is a cause of freedom, and freedom is the right of the mukatab. Once a right is established, it is not extinguished by death, analogous to a debt that survives the creditor's death. The heirs step into the master's place solely for the purpose of collecting the installments of the kitabah payment. This is not a change in the contract but merely a substitution in collection. The text then addresses the scenario where one heir tries to manumit the mukatab individually. According to the Hanafi school, this is ineffective because the mukatab is not owned by any of the heirs individually; the mukatab is not subject to ownership through any cause, including inheritance. The text contrasts this with the Shafi'i position, quoting from Sharh al-Aqta' that Imam al-Shafi'i in one opinion allows a single heir to manumit the mukatab because, in his school, the mukatab can be sold and owned by the master. The Hanafi position relies on the principle that the mukatab is not owned. However, if all the heirs collectively manumit the mukatab, the ruling by qiyas (analogy) would be that it is still invalid because they do not own him. But by istihsan (juristic preference), it is valid and the mukatab becomes free, and the kitabah payment is dropped. The reason for istihsan is that the collective manumission is effectively a discharge from the debt of the kitabah payment, which is their right. Since they have inherited the right to the payment, they can forgo it. Once the debt is discharged, the mukatab is free, just as if the master had released him from the debt. The text concludes by addressing a potential objection: why does a single heir's manumission not have a similar effect, since it could be seen as a discharge from his share? The answer is that the discharge implied by manumission is for the entire debt, not a partial share. Manumission cannot be established partially; it either exists wholly or not at all. Therefore, only the collective act of all heirs can effect manumission through the mechanism of discharge. This passage is a classic example of Hanafi use of qiyas and istihsan in the context of contracts of emancipation.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract of kitabah with his master to earn his freedom by paying a specified sum.
بدل کتابت (badal al-kitabah): The payment (installments) owed by the mukatab to the master under the kitabah contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens to the kitabah contract when the master dies?
A) The contract is void and the mukatab becomes free.
B) The contract is void and the mukatab returns to slavery.
C) The contract remains valid and the mukatab must pay the heirs.
D) The contract remains valid and the mukatab is freed without further payment.

Key Takeaway
The master's death does not void the kitabah contract; the mukatab continues paying installments to the heirs, just as a debtor pays the creditor's heirs.

10 min
Manumission of the Mukatab by the Heirs
Explains Hanafi ruling on manumission of mukatab by heirs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi ruling that a single heir cannot manumit the mukatab, while collective manumission by all heirs is valid by istihsan, and evaluate the opposing Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
One heir cannot free the mukatab; all heirs together can, by discharging the kitabah debt.

When the master dies, the heirs inherit the right to collect the kitabah payment. Can they manumit the mukatab? The Hanafi school distinguishes between individual and collective manumission. A single heir's attempt is ineffective because the mukatab is not owned. However, if all heirs collectively manumit him, it is considered a discharge of the debt (their right), and the mukatab becomes free. This ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference) overriding qiyas. The Shafi'i school, in one view, allows a single heir to manumit because they consider the mukatab ownable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text addresses two cases: (1) one heir manumits the mukatab, (2) all heirs manumit him collectively.
The rulings differ: first invalid, second valid by istihsan.
2
Understand why one heir cannot manumit
The mukatab is not owned through any cause of ownership, so he is not inherited. Therefore, no single heir has ownership to effect manumission.
This is based on the principle that manumission requires ownership of the slave.
3
Apply qiyas to the collective case
By strict analogy (qiyas), even collective manumission would be invalid because the mukatab is not owned.
Qiyas would suggest impossibility.
4
Apply istihsan to the collective case
By istihsan, collective manumission is valid because it is effectively a discharge (ibra') of the kitabah debt, which the heirs have the right to waive.
This overrides qiyas in favor of a more equitable outcome.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i in one opinion holds that a single heir can manumit because he considers the mukatab ownable (sale valid).
The thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference in inheritance planning.

تشریح قوله واذا امات ... الخ - اگر مکاتب کا آقا مر جائے تو کتابت فسخ نہ ہوگی ۔ تا کہ اس کا نتیجہ یہ نہ ہو کہ مکاتب کا حق مٹ جائے ۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ کتابت آزادی کا سبب ہے اور آزادی مکاتب کا حق ہے اور کسی شخص کے حق کا جو سبب ہو وہ بھی اس کا حق ہو جاتا ہے پس کتابت اس کا حق ہوا۔ اور موت کی وجہ سے حق باطل نہیں ہوتا جیسے کسی کا دوسرے کے ذمہ قرض ہوا اور صاحب قرض مرجائے تو قرض باطل نہیں ہو جاتا۔ قوله وقيل له الخ - اب مکاتب مذکور سے کہا جائے گا کہ آقا کے ورثہ کو بدل کتابت مقسطون کے مطابق ادا کر اس لئے کہ وہ آزادی کا مستحق اسی طور پر ہوا تھا او اسی طریقہ پر سبب منعقد ہوا تھا تو وہ اس صفت پر باقی رہے گا اور اس میں کوئی تغیر نہ ہوگا۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ آقا جب صحیح و تندرست ہو تو اس کا کل بدل کتابت کو مؤ جل کرنے کا تصرف صحیح ہوتا ہے جیسے کل بدل کتابت ساقط کرنے کا تصرف صحیح ہے اور یہاں مسئلہ کی وضع چونکہ علی الاطلاق ہے اس سے معلوم ہو گیا کہ آقا صحیح تندرست تھا لہذا اس کا تصرف صحیح ہوا بخلاف اس کے جب آقا مریض ہو اور وہ غلام کو مکاتب کرے کہ اس صورت میں مکاتب یا تو فی الحال اپنی دو تہائی قیمت ادا کرے گا یا اس کو رقیق کر دیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ مریض ہونے کی صورت میں آقا کا تصرف تاجیل واسقاط تہائی کے علاوہ میں صحیح نہیں ہوتا۔ قوله الا ان الورثه الخ -قول سابق ولا يتغیر “ سے استثناء ہے اور گو ایک سوال کا جواب ہے ۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ سبب حریت کیسے متغیر نہ ہو گا جب کہ آقا کا حق استیفاء بدل تھا جو ورثہ کے لئے ہو گیا اور یہی تغیر ہے۔
جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ آقا کے ورثہ صرف مال کتابت وصول کرنے میں اس کے خلیفہ ہوں گے اور صرف اتنی بات سے نہ حق متغیر ہوتا ہے نہ عقد کتابت ( لانها باقية كما كانت ) جیسے ایک شخص کا کسی کے ذمہ قرض ہو اور صاحب قرض مرجائے تو وصولیابی میں اس کے ورثہ اس کے قائم مقام ہوتے ہیں اور مقروض جیسے مورث کو اڑا کرنے سے بری ہو جاتا ہے ایسے ہی ورثہ کو ادا کرنے سے بری ہو جاتا ہے پس جیسے دیگر تمام دیون میں ورثہ اس کے خلیفہ ہوتے ہیں اور اس کو تغیر نہیں کہا جاتا ایسے ہی دین کتابت میں بھی خلافت کو تغیر نہیں کہا جائیگا۔ قوله فان اعتقه احد الورثة ... الخ - پھر گر آقا کے ورثہ میں سے کسی وارث نے مکاتب مذکور کو آزاد کر دیا تو اس کا آزاد کرنا نافذ نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ اس کا مالک نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ مکاتب اسباب ملک میں سے کسی سبب کے ذریعہ مملوک نہیں ہوتا۔ ولا عتق فيما لا یملکہ ابن آدم شرح اقطع میں ہے کہ امام شافعی کے ایک قول میں اس کا آزاد کرنا نافذ ہو جائے گا۔ لانه يصح عنده بيع المكاتب ويصح ان يملك آقا
قوله فان اعتقوه جميعاً ... الخ - اور اگر اس کو سب ورثہ نے آزاد کر دیا تو مقتضائے قیاس تو یہی ہے کہ اب بھی جائز نہ ہو۔ کیونکہ ان کا تصرف اس کی طرف مضاف ہوا ہے جو ان کی ملک نہیں ہے۔ لیکن استحسانا آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ اور اس کے ذمہ سے بدل کتابت ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ ان سب کا آزاد کرنا بدل کتابت سے بری کرنا ہے کیونکہ عوض مذکور ان کا حق ہے جس میں وراثت جاری ہو چکی تو ان کو اپنا حق چھوڑ دینے کا اختیار ہے۔ اور جب مکاتب عوض کتابت سے بری ہو گیا۔ تو وہ آزاد ہو جائے گا جیسے اگر خود اس کو بری کرتا تو وہ آزاد ہو جاتا۔ ممکن ہے کوئی یہ کہے کہ ایک کے آزاد کرنے سے بھی آزاد ہو جانا چاہیے کیونکہ ایک کا آزاد کرنا اپنے حصہ سے بری کرنا ہے۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ یہ نہیں ہو سکتا۔ کیونکہ ہم نے جواعتقاق کو ابراہ قرار دیا ہے وہ تھے حق کے لئے بطریق اقتضاء کیا ہے اور بعض کے بری کرنے یا ادا کرنے سے مکاتب میں اعتاق ثابت نہیں ہوتا نہ اس کے جزء میں نہ کل میں۔
Book of the Mukatab. Freedom is a cause, and also a cause of a person's right is his right. The mukatab will be told: 'Pay the master's heirs according to your installments, because he became deserving of freedom in this manner and the cause was contracted in this manner, so it will remain in that state, unchanged, except that the heirs become his successors in collection. Then if one of the heirs manumits him, his manumission is not effective because he is not his owner, and the reason is that the mukatab is not owned through other causes of ownership, so likewise by inheritance it will not occur. Yes, if all heirs manumit him, he becomes free and the kitabah payment is dropped, because this is a discharge from the kitabah payment, since the consideration is their right and inheritance has taken effect. So when he is discharged from the kitabah payment, he becomes free, just as if the master had discharged him. But if one heir manumits him, this is not a discharge from his share, because we establish discharge by implication for the validity of his manumission, and manumission is not established in the mukatab by the discharge or payment of some, neither in whole nor in part, and there is no degree of making it a discharge of the whole due to the right of the remaining heirs. And Allah knows best. Explanation of his statement: 'And when the master dies...' etc. If the master of the mukatab dies, the kitabah is not rescinded, so that the mukatab's right is not eliminated. The reason is that kitabah is a cause of freedom, and freedom is the right of the mukatab, and whatever is a cause of a person's right also becomes his right. Thus kitabah became his right, and death does not invalidate a right, just as if someone has a debt on another and the creditor dies, the debt is not invalidated. His statement: 'And it will be said to him...' etc. Now the aforementioned mukatab will be told to pay the heirs the kitabah payment according to the installments, because he became deserving of freedom in this manner and the cause was contracted in this manner, so it will remain in that state and there will be no change. The reason is that when the master is healthy, his act of deferring the entire kitabah payment is valid, just as his act of dropping the entire kitabah payment is valid, and here the case is absolute, so it is known that the master was healthy, hence his act is valid, contrary to when the master is ill and he makes the slave a mukatab, in which case the mukatab will either pay two-thirds of his value immediately or he will be re-enslaved, because in the case of illness the master's act of deferral and dropping other than one-third is not valid. His statement: 'Except that the heirs...' etc. This is an exception from the previous statement 'and it does not change', and it is also an answer to a question. The question is: How does the cause of freedom not change when the master's right to receive the payment becomes for the heirs, and this is a change? The summary of the answer is that the master's heirs are only his successors in collecting the kitabah payment, and by this alone neither the right nor the contract of kitabah changes (because it remains as it was), just as if a person has a debt on someone and the creditor dies, in collection his heirs stand in his place, and the debtor is discharged by paying the heirs just as he would be discharged by paying the ancestor. So just as in all other debts the heirs are successors and this is not called a change, likewise in the debt of kitabah, the succession is not called a change. His statement: 'If one of the heirs manumits him...' etc. Then if one of the master's heirs manumits the aforementioned mukatab, his manumission is not effective because he is not his owner, since the mukatab is not owned through any cause of ownership. And there is no manumission in what a person does not own. In Sharh al-Aqta' it is stated that in one of Imam al-Shafi'i's opinions, his manumission would be effective because according to him the sale of the mukatab is valid and the master can own him. His statement: 'If they all manumit him...' etc. If all heirs manumit him, the logical requirement (qiyas) is that it is still not valid because their act pertains to someone not in their ownership. However, by istihsan, he becomes free and the kitabah payment is dropped from his liability. The reason for istihsan is that their collective manumission is a discharge from the kitabah payment because the said consideration is their right in which inheritance has taken effect, so they have the option to relinquish their right. And when the mukatab is discharged from the kitabah payment, he becomes free, just as if the master himself had discharged him. It is possible that someone might say that manumission by one should also free him because one's manumission is a discharge from his share. The answer is that this cannot be, because we have established manumission as a discharge by implication for the whole right, and manumission is not established in the mukatab by the discharge or payment of some, neither in part nor in whole.
