قوله وهذا بخلاف ما .... الخ - حكم مذكور ولاء موالات کے خلاف ہے۔ مثلاً شوہر وزوجہ نے مسلمان ہو کر متفرق موالات کی بائیں طور کہ زوجہ نے ایک شخص (زید) سے موالات کی ۔ درانحالیلہ وہ حاملہ ہے۔ اور اس کے شوہر نے دوسرے شخص ( بکر ) سے موالات کی تو بچہ کی ولاء اس کے لئے ہوگی جس سے باپ نے موالات کی ہے۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ شکمی بچہ بالقصد ایسی موالات کرنے کے قابل نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ یہ موالات ایجاب و قبول سے پوری ہوتی ہے اور بچہ اس کا محل نہیں ہے بخلاف ولا عتاقہ کے کہ اس میں جنین مقصود بالا عتاق ہو جاتا ہے۔ لانہ محل لاضافة العتق اليه و بعد ماصار مقصود الا يمكن ان يجعل تابعاً لغيره في الولاء قوله نان ولدت بعد عتقها ... الخ - اور اگر مذکورہ باندی اپنے آزاد ہو جانے سے چھ ماہ سے زیادہ پر بچہ جنے تو اس کی ولاء بھی اس کی ماں کے آقا کو ملے گی (بشرطیکہ اس کا باپ آزاد نہ ہو گیا ہو جیسا کہ اگلے مسئلے میں آرہا ہے ) وجہ یہ ہے کہ وہ بچہ اپنی ماں کی تبعیت میں آزاد ہو گیا کیونکہ ماں کی آزدی کے بعد وہ ماں کے ساتھ متصل ہے تو ولاء میں بھی ماں کا تابع ہوگا۔ اور اعتاق کے وقت حمل قائم ہونے کا تیقن نہیں ہے تا کہ بالقصد آزاد ہو جائے۔ جیسا کہ پہلی صورت میں تھا۔ فلا جرم عتق تبعاً لھا
A slave of one person married a slave woman of another, then the master of the slave woman freed her while she was pregnant from the slave; she becomes free and her pregnancy also becomes free, and the wala' of the child belongs to the master of the mother, never to be transferred from him. And if a slave of a man marries a slave woman of another, and the master of the slave woman frees her while she is pregnant from the slave, she becomes free and her child becomes free, and the wala' of the child belongs to the master of the mother, never to be transferred from him, because he was freed as a direct intention upon the emancipator of the mother, as he is a part of her that is capable of being the direct object of emancipation, so his wala' is not transferred from him, acting upon what we have narrated. Similarly, if she gives birth to a child within less than six months, due to certainty of the pregnancy existing at the time of emancipation, or she gives birth to two children, one of which is within less than six months, because they are twins connected together. And this is contrary to when a woman enters into a contract of wala' (muwalat) while she is pregnant and the husband enters into it with another, the wala' of the child goes to the master of the father, because the fetus is not capable of being the direct object of this wala', because its completion requires offer and acceptance, and the fetus is not a subject for it. He said: If she gives birth after her emancipation after more than six months to a child, then his wala' is for the masters of the mother, because he was freed as a dependent of the mother due to his connection with her after her emancipation, so he follows her in wala', and his existence at the time of emancipation is not certain so that he would be freed as a direct intention. Translation: If a slave of someone marries a slave woman of another, then the master of the slave woman frees her while she is pregnant from the slave, she becomes free and her child also becomes free, and the wala' of the child goes to the master of the mother, never to be transferred from him, because... [PAGE_208] Book of Wala'. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume 12. He was freed as a direct intention upon the emancipator of the mother, because he is a part of the mother capable of being the direct object of emancipation, so his wala' will not be transferred from him, acting upon the hadith that we narrated. Similarly, if she gives birth to a child within less than six months, due to certainty of the pregnancy existing at the time of emancipation, or she gives birth to two children, one of which is within less than six months, because they are twins whose existence together is established. And this is contrary to when a wife enters into a contract of wala' (muwalat) with someone while she is pregnant, and the husband enters into it with another person, then the wala' of the child is for the one with whom the father contracted, because the fetal child is not capable of being the direct object of such wala', because this wala' is completed by offer and acceptance, and the fetus is not a subject for it. Then if the slave woman gives birth after her emancipation after more than six months to a child, then his wala' is for the masters of the mother, because he was freed as a dependent of the mother, due to his connection with her after her emancipation, so he follows her in wala', and the existence of the pregnancy at the time of emancipation is not certain, so he is not freed as a direct intention. Explanation of his statement: 'And if he marries... etc.' The issue is: Zaid has a slave and Bakr has a slave woman. So Zaid's slave married Bakr's slave woman with permission in a valid marriage. Then Bakr freed his slave woman while she was pregnant from the slave. The ruling is that the slave woman becomes free and her child also becomes free, and the wala' of the child goes to the master of the mother, not to the master of the father, because the child is a part of the mother, and the master of the mother has applied emancipation to all her parts with direct intention, and the child is capable of being the direct object of emancipation, so he is freed by the emancipator of the mother. Therefore, his wala' is not transferred to the master of the father, because the wala' established by text (hadith) for the emancipator is absolute, so it is acted upon. His statement: 'Similarly, if she gives birth... etc.' Similarly, if that slave woman gives birth within less than six months after her freedom, then also the wala' of that child goes to the master of the mother, because the existence of pregnancy at the time of freedom is certain. Also, if she gives birth to two children, one of which is within less than six months, then also the wala' of both goes to the master of the mother, because they are twins whose conception occurred together, i.e., the existence of both pregnancies at the time of freedom is certain. His statement: 'And this is contrary to what... etc.' The mentioned ruling is contrary to wala' of muwalat. For example, a husband and wife became Muslim and contracted separate wala' (muwalat) in this way: the wife contracted wala' with one person (Zaid) while she was pregnant, and her husband contracted wala' with another person (Bakr). Then the child's wala' will be for the one with whom the father contracted. The reason is that the fetal child is not capable of being the direct object of such wala', because this wala' is completed by offer and acceptance, and the child is not a subject for it, contrary to wala' of emancipation, where the fetus becomes the direct object of emancipation. His statement: 'If she gives birth after her emancipation... etc.' And if the mentioned slave woman gives birth after more than six months from her emancipation, then her child's wala' also goes to the mother's master (provided that her father has not become free, as will come in the next issue). The reason is that the child was freed as a dependent of his mother, because after the mother's freedom, he is connected to her, so in wala' he will follow her. And the existence of the pregnancy at the time of emancipation is not certain, so that he would be freed as a direct intention, as in the first case. Therefore, he was freed as a dependent of her.
Source pages p. 207

Commentary
This passage provides a detailed Hanafi ruling on the wala' (clientage) of a child born to a slave woman who is freed while pregnant. The key principle is that when a pregnant slave woman is freed, her unborn child is also freed because he is considered a part of her. Consequently, the child's wala' belongs exclusively to the mother's former master (the emancipator), not to the father's master. This is based on the hadith that wala' belongs to the one who sets free (al-wala' li man a'taqa). The passage elaborates on three scenarios: (1) The child is born within six months of the mother's emancipation, confirming that the pregnancy existed at the time of emancipation; (2) The mother gives birth to twins, one born within six months; (3) The child is born after six months, in which case the child is freed as a dependent of the mother, and his wala' still goes to the mother's master, unless the father had been freed earlier (as will be discussed later). The passage also distinguishes this from wala' by contract (muwalat), where a fetus cannot enter into such a contract because it requires offer and acceptance, so in that case the child's wala' follows the father's muwali.

Key Terms
حمل (haml): The unborn child (fetus) in the womb.
ولاء (wala'): The bond of clientage that gives the former master inheritance rights and responsibility for blood money.
موالات (muwalat): A contract of clientage between two free persons, establishing mutual inheritance and responsibility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A slave woman owned by Bakr, married to Zaid's slave, is freed by Bakr while she is pregnant. She gives birth after seven months. Who gets the wala' of the child?
A) Zaid (the father's master)
B) Bakr (the mother's master)
C) The child himself
D) The Muslim community

Key Takeaway
The wala' of a child born to a freed pregnant slave woman belongs exclusively to the mother's emancipator, as the child is freed as part of the mother.

Wala' of a Child Born to a Freed Slave Woman
Explaining the wala' of a child born to a freed slave woman

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the wala' of a child born to a freed slave woman and identify the conditions that determine whether the wala' goes to the mother's patron or the father's patron.

Core Idea
The child's wala' follows the mother's patron if pregnancy existed at manumission; otherwise it may be transferable.

This lesson from Ashraf al-Hidayah explains the complex rulings of wala' for a child born to a freed slave woman. The key factor is whether the child was in the womb at the time of the mother's manumission. We will examine the scenarios, the reasoning, and the distinction between intentional and followership manumission. Understanding this helps clarify inheritance rights in such cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Freeing a pregnant slave woman. The ruling: the child becomes free and its wala' goes to the mother's patron.
The wala' is a right of inheritance for the manumitter.
2
Locate the underlying principle
The child is considered a part (juz') of the mother. Therefore, when the mother is freed intentionally (bil-qasd), the child is also freed intentionally, and its wala' cannot transfer to the father's patron.
This is based on a hadith that wala' is like lineage.
3
Apply the condition of certainty of pregnancy
If the child is born within six months of manumission, the pregnancy at that time is certain. If born after six months, the pregnancy is uncertain, and the child is freed by followership (bi al-tabi'ah).
In followership, the wala' is transferable (e.g., if the father is later freed).
4
Contrast with muwalat (contractual patronage)
If a wife contracts muwalat while pregnant, the unborn child cannot be a party; thus the child's wala' follows the father's patron after birth.
Muwalat requires offer and acceptance, which a fetus cannot perform.
5
Distinguish between intentional and followership manumission
In intentional manumission (first case), the child's wala' is fixed to the mother's patron. In followership (second case), the wala' still goes to the mother's patron but is transferable if the father becomes free.
This distinction affects whether the wala' can later be transferred.

كتاب الولاء
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲ وہ ماں کے آزاد کنندہ پر بالقصد آزاد ہوا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ وہ ماں کا جزء ہے جو بالنقصد اعتناق کے قابل ہے تو اس کی ولا ، آقات منتقل نہ ہو گی عمل کرتے ہوئے اس حدیث پر جو ہم نے روایت کی ۔ ایسے ہی جب اس نے بچہ جنا چھ ماہ سے کم میں بوقت اعتناق قیام تمل متیقن ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ یاوہ دو بچے بنے ، جن میں سے ایک چھ ماہ سے کم میں ہے کیونکہ وہ دونوں جڑواں ہیں کہ ان کا عمل ایک ساتھ رہا ہے۔ اور یہ اس کے خلاف ہے جب زوجہ نے کسی سے موالات کی درانحالیکہ وہ حاملہ ہے اور شوہر نے کسی دوسرے شخص سے موالات کی کہ بچہ کی ولاء موالی اب کے لئے ہوگی۔ کیونکہ حکمی بچہ بالقصد ایسی موالات کے قابل نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ اس موالات کا پورا ہونا ایجاب وقبول سے ہوتا ہے اور جنین اس کا محل نہیں ہے ۔ پھر اگر باندی نے اپنے آزاد ہونے کے بعد چھ ماہ سے زائد پر بچہ جنا تو اس کی ولاء موالی ام کے لئے ہوگی کیونکہ وہ ماں کی تبیعت پر آزاد ہو گیا۔ ماں کی آزادی کے بعد اس کے ساتھ متصل ہونے کی وجہ سے تو ولاء میں بھی اس کا تابع ہوگا اور بوقت اعتاق قیام حمل کا تیقین نہیں ہے۔ تا کہ بالقصد آزاد ہو جائے۔
تشریح قوله واذا تزوج .. الخ ۔ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ زید کا ایک غلام ہے اور بکر کی ایک باندی ہے۔ پس زید کے خانم مکر کی باندی سے باجازت نکاح صحیح کر لیا پھر بکر نے اپنی باندی کو اس حالت میں کہ وہ غلام سے حاملہ ہے آزاد کر دیا تو حکم یہ ہے کہ باندی آزاد ہو جائے گی اور اس کا حمل بھی آزاد ہو جائے گا اور حمل کی ولاء اس کی ماں کے آقا کو ملے گی۔ اس کے باپ کے آقا کو نہیں ملے گی اس واسطے کہ حمل بھی ماں کا ایک جزء ہے اور ماں کے آقا نے بالقصد اس کے جمیع اجزاء پر عتق کو واقع کیا اور وہ بالقصد اعتناق کے قابل بھی ہے تو وہ بھی ماں کے آزاد کرنے والے کی طرف سے بالقصد آزاد ہوا لہذا اس کی ولاء باپ کے آقا کی طرف منتقل نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ آزادکنندہ کے لئے ولاء کا ثابت ہو نا نص میں مطلق ہے تو اس پر عمل ہوگا۔
قوله وكذلك اذا ولدت الخ - اسی طرح اگر وہ باندی اپنی آزادی کے بعد چھ ماہ سے کم میں بچہ جنے تب بھی اس بچہ کی ولاء اس کی ماں کے آقا کو ملے گی ۔ کیونکہ آزادی کے وقت حمل کا ہونا متیقین ہے۔ نیز اگر وہ باندی دو بچے جنے جن میں ایک بچہ چھ ماہ سے کم میں ہے ۔ تب بھی ان دونوں کی ولاء ماں کے آقا کو ملے گی ۔ کیونکہ یہ دونوں بچے جڑواں ہیں جن کا اقرار ایک ساتھ ہوا ہے یعنی آزادی کے وقت دونوں کے حمل کا ہونا متیقن ہے۔
قوله وهذا بخلاف ما .... الخ - حكم مذكور ولاء موالات کے خلاف ہے۔ مثلاً شوہر وزوجہ نے مسلمان ہو کر متفرق موالات کی بائیں طور کہ زوجہ نے ایک شخص (زید) سے موالات کی ۔ درانحالیلہ وہ حاملہ ہے۔ اور اس کے شوہر نے دوسرے شخص ( بکر ) سے موالات کی تو بچہ کی ولاء اس کے لئے ہوگی جس سے باپ نے موالات کی ہے۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ شکمی بچہ بالقصد ایسی موالات کرنے کے قابل نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ یہ موالات ایجاب و قبول سے پوری ہوتی ہے اور بچہ اس کا محل نہیں ہے بخلاف ولا عتاقہ کے کہ اس میں جنین مقصود بالا عتاق ہو جاتا ہے۔ لانہ محل لاضافة العتق اليه و بعد ماصار مقصود الا يمكن ان يجعل تابعاً لغيره في الولاء قوله نان ولدت بعد عتقها ... الخ - اور اگر مذکورہ باندی اپنے آزاد ہو جانے سے چھ ماہ سے زیادہ پر بچہ جنے تو اس کی ولاء بھی اس کی ماں کے آقا کو ملے گی (بشرطیکہ اس کا باپ آزاد نہ ہو گیا ہو جیسا کہ اگلے مسئلے میں آرہا ہے ) وجہ یہ ہے کہ وہ بچہ اپنی ماں کی تبعیت میں آزاد ہو گیا کیونکہ ماں کی آزدی کے بعد وہ ماں کے ساتھ متصل ہے تو ولاء میں بھی ماں کا تابع ہوگا۔ اور اعتاق کے وقت حمل قائم ہونے کا تیقن نہیں ہے تا کہ بالقصد آزاد ہو جائے۔ جیسا کہ پہلی صورت میں تھا۔ فلا جرم عتق تبعاً لھا ۔
فائدہ دونوں صورتوں میں فرق یہ ہوا کہ پہلی صورت میں جب کہ بوقت اعتاق حمل موجود ہے یا بچہ چھ ماہ سے کم پر جنا جس سے اعتاق کے وقت موجود ہونے کا تیقن ہے تو اس صورت میں بچہ بالقصد آزد کیا گیا ہے اور آزاد کنندہ وہی آتا ہے جس نے اس کی ماں کو آزاد کیا ہے پس آزاد کنندہ سے ولاء منقول نہ ہوگی۔ اور اس دوسری صورت میں جب آزدی کے وقت سے چھ ماہ سے زیادہ پر جنا ہے جس سے بوقت اعتاق حمل موجود ہونے کا تیقین نہیں ہے تو اس صورت میں بچہ کی آزادی قصدا نہ ہوگی بلکہ ماں کی تبعیت میں ہوگی حتی کہ یہ ولاء قابل انتقال ہے۔ اگر چہ با فعل اس کی ولاء ماں کے آقا کے لئے ہوگی۔
(Book of Wala') Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary of Hidayah Volume 12. And he was freed intentionally by the mother's manumitter, because he is a part of the mother which is capable of being intended for manumission. So his wala' will not be transferred to the father's patron, acting upon this hadith that we narrated. Similarly, when she gave birth to a child in less than six months, at the time of manumission the existence of the pregnancy is certain. Or if she gave birth to two children, one of whom is in less than six months because they are twins, their creation occurred together. And this is contrary to the case when a wife contracted muwalat with someone while she was pregnant, and the husband contracted muwalat with another person: the child's wala' will be for the father's mawla. Because the unborn child is not capable of such muwalat intentionally, because the completion of muwalat occurs through offer and acceptance, and the fetus is not a locus for it. Then if the slave woman gave birth after more than six months from her manumission, her wala' will be for the mother's mawla because he became free by following the mother. Since he was attached to her after her freedom, so in wala' he will be a follower of her, and at the time of manumission the existence of the pregnancy is not certain so that he would be freed intentionally. (Commentary on 'And if he married...') The issue is that Zaid has a slave and Bakr has a slave woman. Zaid's slave married Bakr's slave woman with permission, then Bakr freed his slave woman while she was pregnant from the slave. The ruling is that the slave woman becomes free and her fetus also becomes free, and the wala' of the fetus will go to his mother's master, not to his father's master. Because the fetus is a part of the mother, and the mother's master intentionally applied manumission to all her parts, and it is capable of being intended for manumission. So he was also freed intentionally by the mother's manumitter, hence his wala' will not transfer to the father's master. Because the establishment of wala' for the manumitter is absolute in the text, so it is acted upon. (Commentary on 'Similarly when she gives birth...') Similarly, if that slave woman gave birth within less than six months after her manumission, then the wala' of that child will go to his mother's master, because at the time of manumission the existence of pregnancy is certain. Also, if that slave woman gave birth to two children, one of whom is within less than six months, then the wala' of both will go to the mother's master, because these two children are twins whose formation occurred together, i.e., at the time of manumission the existence of pregnancy for both is certain. (Commentary on 'And this is contrary to...') The mentioned ruling is contrary to the wala' of muwalat. For example, a husband and wife both accepted Islam and contracted muwalat separately: the wife contracted muwalat with one person (Zaid) while she was pregnant, and her husband contracted muwalat with another person (Bakr). Then the child's wala' will be for the one with whom the father contracted muwalat. The reason is that the unborn child is not capable of such muwalat intentionally, because muwalat is completed through offer and acceptance, and the child is not a locus for it, contrary to the wala' of manumission where the fetus becomes intended for manumission because it is a locus for the addition of manumission to it, and after it becomes intended, it cannot be made a follower of others in wala'. (Commentary on 'And if she gave birth after her manumission...') And if the aforementioned slave woman gave birth after more than six months from her manumission, then her wala' will also go to her mother's master (provided that her father has not been freed, as will come in the next issue). The reason is that the child became free by following his mother, because after the mother's freedom he is attached to her, so in wala' he will be a follower of the mother. And at the time of manumission the existence of the pregnancy is not certain so that he would be freed intentionally, as in the first case. Hence he is freed following her. Benefit: The difference between the two cases is that in the first case, when the pregnancy is present at the time of manumission or the child is born within less than six months indicating certain existence at that time, then the child is freed intentionally and the manumitter is the same who freed the mother, so the wala' will not be transferred from the manumitter. In the second case, when the child is born after more than six months from manumission, so the existence of the pregnancy at the time of manumission is not certain, then the child's freedom is not intentional but rather in followership of the mother, so this wala' is transferable. Nevertheless, practically his wala' will be for the mother's master.
Source pages p. 208

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is a commentary (sharh) on al-Hidayah, explaining the rulings regarding the wala' (clientage) of a child born to a slave woman who is freed while pregnant. The text presents several scenarios and provides the Hanafi position. The key principle is that the child's wala' follows the mother's patron if the child was in utero at the time of the mother's manumission or is born within six months, as this indicates certain existence at that moment. The child is considered a part of the mother (juz'), so the manumission intentionally covers it. Therefore, the wala' cannot transfer to the father's patron. The text contrasts this with muwalat (patronage by contract), where the unborn child cannot be a party; thus, after birth, the child's wala' follows the father's patron. If the child is born after six months, the pregnancy at manumission is uncertain, so the child is freed by following the mother (taba'iyyah), and while its wala' still rests with the mother's patron initially, it becomes transferable (e.g., if the father is later freed). The commentary thoroughly explains each sub-case and the reasoning behind the rulings, emphasizing the distinction between intentional and followership manumission.

Key Terms
ولاء (wala'): The legal clientage relationship established between a manumitter and a freed slave, granting the manumitter the right to inherit from the freed person under certain conditions.
بالقصد (bil-qasd): Intentionally; the manumission of the child is directly intended by the manumitter, as the child is considered a part of the mother.
بالتبع (bi al-tabi'ah): By followership; the child is freed as a consequence of the mother's freedom, not by a separate intention.
موالات (muwalat): A contract of patronage between free persons who are not related, creating a mutual inheritance right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the scenario where a pregnant slave woman is freed, and she gives birth within six months, whose patron gets the wala' of the child?
A) The child's father's patron
B) The child's mother's patron
C) The child's own patron if freed separately
D) The patron of the husband's owner

Key Takeaway
The wala' of a child born to a freed slave woman goes to the mother's patron if the pregnancy was certain at manumission (birth within six months) or by followership if uncertain (birth after six months), with the latter being transferable.

Father's Manumission Transfers Child's Wala' to His Patron
Hanafi ruling with proof and madhhab dispute on wala' transfer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a father's subsequent manumission transfers his child's wala' to his patron, cite the hadith evidence, and compare the opposing view.

Core Idea
When a father is freed, he pulls his child's wala' from the mother's patron because wala' is like lineage, which follows the father.

This lesson examines a key rule in Hanafi wala' jurisprudence: the transfer of wala' when a formerly enslaved father becomes free. The passage clarifies that a child's wala' initially attributed to the mother's patron can shift to the father's patron once the father is eligible. This is based on the Prophetic hadith equating wala' to lineage, which is traced through fathers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the Hanafi position: if the father is freed, he pulls the wala' of his child from the mother's mawali to his own mawali.
This is the core ruling of the passage.
2
Understand the basis
Recognize that the child's freedom was by followership (taba'iyyah) of the mother, not intentional; thus wala' is not firmly fixed to the mother's patron.
This distinguishes this case from where the child is freed directly.
3
Analyze the dalil
Examine the hadith: 'al-wala' luhmah ka-luhmi al-nasab' – wala' is a bond like lineage. Since lineage is traced through fathers, wala' follows similarly.
The hadith emphasizes permanence but also paternal attribution.
4
Apply the analogy
Consider the child of li'an: initially ascribed to mother's clan out of necessity, but reverts to father when paternity is established. This supports the transfer when the father becomes eligible.
The necessity here is the father's slavery; when removed, the natural attribution returns.
5
Contrast the opposing view
Some scholars hold that wala' is fixed once established and cannot transfer. Understand their reasoning and the Hanafi response.
The thamarah al-khilaf affects inheritance rights from the child.

فان أعتق الاب جرّ الاب ولاء ابنه وانتقل عن موالى الام الى موالى الاب لان العتق ههنا في الولد يثبت تبعا للام بخلاف الأول وهذا لان الولاء بمنزلة النسب قال عليه السلام الولاء لحمة كلحمة النسب لا يباع ولا يوهب ولا يورث ثم النسب الى الآباء فكذلك الولاء والنسبة الى موالى الام كانت لعدم أهلية الاب ضرورة فاذا صار اهلا عاد الولاء اليه بمنزلة ولد الملاعنة يُنسب الى قوم الام ضرورة فاذا كذب الملاعن عن نفسه يُنسب اليه
ترجمہ پھر اگر آزاد کر دیا گیا تو باپ کھینچ لے گا باپ اپنے بیٹے کی ولاء اور منتقل ہو جائے گی موالی ام سے موالی اب کی طرف۔ کیونکہ یہاں بچہ میں آزادی ماں کی تعبیعت میں ثابت ہوئی بخلاف پہلی صورت کے ، اور یہ اس لئے کہ ولاء بمنزلہ نسب کے ہے حضور علیہ السلام نے ارشاد فرمایا۔ ولاء قرابت ہے قرابت نسب کی طرح نہ بیچی جائے گی نہ ہبہ کی جائے گی اس میں وراثت جاری ہوگی ۔ پھر نسب آباء کی جانب ہوتا ہے تو ایسے کے لاء ہوگی ۔ اور موالی ام کی طرف نسبت باپ کی عدم اہلیت کی ضرورت سے تھی جب باپ اس لائق ہو گیا تو ولاء اس کی طرف لوٹ آئی بمنزلہ ملا عنہ عورت کے بچہ کے کہ بوجہ ضرورت ماں کی قوم کی طرف منسوب ہوا اور جب لعان کنندہ نے خود کو جھٹلا دیا تو اسی کی طرف منسوب ہو جائے گا۔
تشریح قوله فان اعتق الاب .... الخ - اور اگر بچہ کا باپ آزاد کر دیا گیا تو اب وہ بچہ کی ولاء اپنی طرف کھینچ لے گا اور ولاء موالی ام سے منتقل ہو کر موالی اب کی طرف چلی جائے گی ۔ جمہور صحابہ کرام و تابعین عظام - حضرت عمر ، عثمان علی، زبیر، عبداللہ ، زید بن ثابت، مردان سعید بن المسیب ، حسن بصری ، ابن سیرین، عمر بن عبد العزیز، ابراہیم نخعی سے یہی مروی ہے اور سفیان تو رسی ،لیث بن سعد، الحق بن راہویہ، ابوثور، ائمہ ثلاثہ اور احناف اسی کے قائل ہیں۔ اس کے بر خلاف مالک بن اوس بن حدثان ، ابن شہاب زہری ، داؤد ظاہری، میمون بن مہران اور حمید بن عبد الرحمن کے نزدیک ولاء موالی ام سے منتقل نہیں ہوگی ۔ حضرت عثمان اور زید بن ثابت سے بھی اسی طرح کی روایت ہے۔ لیکن ابن اللبان نے اس کا انکار کیا ہے۔ قوله لان الولاء بمنزله النسب .. الخ - ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد ہے الولاء لحمة اھا کہ ولاء ایک قرابت ہے قرابت نسب کی طرح نہ اس کو فروخت کیا جا سکتا ہے نہ ہبہ اور نہ اس میں وراثت جاری ہو سکتی ہے پھر نسب چونکہ بجانب آباء ہوتا ہے۔ تو ایسے ہی ملا ر بھی آباء کی طرف ہو گی ۔ پہلی صورت میں جو نسب موالی ام کی طرف ہو گئی تھی وہ باپ کی عدم اہلبیت کی وجہ سے تھی
(Section on pulling wala') If the father is freed, the father pulls the wala' of his son, and it transfers from the mother's mawali to the father's mawali, because the manumission here is established in the child as a follower of the mother, contrary to the first [case]. And this is because wala' is like lineage; the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Wala' is a bond like the bond of lineage: it is not sold, not gifted, and not inherited.' Then lineage is to fathers, so likewise wala' is [to fathers]. And the attribution to the mother's mawali was due to the father's lack of eligibility out of necessity, so when he becomes eligible, the wala' returns to him, like the child of a woman subjected to li'an: he is attributed to the mother's people out of necessity, and when the one who performed li'an denies [paternity] from himself, he is attributed to him. Translation: Then if [the father] is freed, the father will pull the wala' of his son, and it will transfer from the mother's mawali to the father's mawali, because here the child's freedom is established in followership of the mother, contrary to the first case. And this is because wala' is like lineage; the Prophet (peace be upon him) stated: 'Wala' is a kinship like kinship of lineage; it will not be sold, nor gifted, and inheritance will pass through it.' Then lineage is from the father's side, so likewise wala' will be. And the attribution to the mother's mawali was due to necessity because of the father's lack of eligibility. When the father becomes eligible, the wala' returns to him, like the child of a woman subjected to li'an: he is attributed to the mother's people due to necessity, and when the one who performed li'an denies [paternity] from himself, he is attributed to him. Commentary on 'If the father is freed...' - If the child's father is freed, then he will pull the child's wala' to himself, and the wala' will transfer from the mother's mawali to the father's mawali. This is narrated from the majority of the Companions and the great Successors: 'Umar, 'Uthman, 'Ali, al-Zubayr, 'Abdullah, Zayd ibn Thabit, [and] Sa'id ibn al-Musayyab, al-Hasan al-Basri, Ibn Sirin, 'Umar ibn 'Abd al-'Aziz, Ibrahim al-Nakha'i - and Sufyan al-Thawri, Layth ibn Sa'd, Ishaq ibn Rahwayh, Abu Thawr, the three Imams [Abu Hanifa, Malik, al-Shafi'i? Actually 'the three Imams' likely refers to Abu Hanifa, Malik, and Ahmad] and the Hanafis hold this view. Contrary to this, Malik ibn Aws ibn Hadathan, Ibn Shihab al-Zuhri, Dawud al-Zahiri, Maymun ibn Mihran, and Humayd ibn 'Abd al-Rahman hold that the wala' does not transfer from the mother's mawali. A similar narration is also from 'Uthman and Zayd ibn Thabit, but Ibn al-Laban denied it. Commentary on 'Because wala' is like lineage...' - Our proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) stated: 'Wala' is a bond like the bond of lineage; it cannot be sold, nor gifted, nor can inheritance pass through it.' Then since lineage is towards fathers, so likewise wala' will be towards fathers. In the first case, the attribution to the mother's mawali was due to the father's lack of lineage [freedom].
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah is a commentary that explains the ruling on the transfer of a child's wala' when the father, who was previously a slave, is later manumitted. The text first presents the ruling (matn): if the father is freed, he pulls (jarra) the wala' of his son to his own patron, transferring it from the mother's mawali to his mawali. This is because the child's freedom in this case (when born after six months) was by followership of the mother, not by direct intention, making the wala' transferable. The evidence is the hadith that wala' is like lineage (lahma ka-lahmi al-nasab), and lineage is traced through fathers. Thus, when the father becomes a free person and thus 'eligible' to carry wala', it naturally returns to his side. The text analogizes this to the child from li'an (mutual imprecation), where the child is initially attributed to the mother's clan out of necessity, but if the father acknowledges paternity or the li'an is resolved, the child is attributed back to him. The commentary then lists the scholars who hold this view (the majority of Companions and Successors, including the three Imams and the Hanafis) and those who oppose it (including some early figures and Dawud al-Zahiri), noting that the Hanafi position is the relied-upone view. The passage thus provides a complete legal unit: the ruling, its proof, and the madhhab dispute.

Key Terms
جر الولاء (jarr al-wala'): The legal mechanism by which a father, upon being freed, pulls the wala' of his child from the mother's patron to his own patron.
لحمة (lahmah): A bond or connection; in the hadith, it refers to the close, inseparable relationship of wala' akin to lineage.
ملاعنة (mula'anah): Mutual imprecation between spouses when the husband accuses the wife of adultery and denies paternity; the child is initially attributed to the mother's clan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, what is the basis for the father's ability to pull (jarr) the wala' of his child from the mother's mawali to his mawali?
A) The child's freedom was intentional at the time of the mother's manumission
B) The child's freedom was by followership, and wala' is like lineage which follows the father
C) The father's manumission cancels the mother's manumission
D) The child chooses to follow the father

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that a father's subsequent manumission transfers his child's wala' from the mother's patron to his own patron because wala' follows lineage and the initial attachment was by necessity.

Wala Transferability Based on Timing of Conception
Explains the difference in wala transferability based on timing of conception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two scenarios regarding wala transferability when a child is born after the mother's emancipation and apply the six-month rule to determine transferability.

Core Idea
Certainty of the child's existence at emancipation determines whether wala is transferable.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah clarifies a critical nuance in Hanafi fiqh regarding the wala of a child born after the mother's emancipation. The key distinction hinges on whether the child was conceived before or after the emancipation, which is determined by the time of birth relative to the emancipation. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly assigning wala in such cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two cases: one where the child is born within six months of emancipation (or the fetus is known to exist), and another where the child is born more than six months after emancipation.
2
Understand the six-month rule
A birth within six months indicates conception before emancipation, making the child's existence at emancipation certain. A birth after six months indicates conception after emancipation, so existence is uncertain.
Six months is the minimum period of pregnancy in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Determine wala transferability
In the first scenario, the child is freed intentionally along with the mother, so wala belongs to the mother's master and is not transferable. In the second, the child's freedom is not intentional but follows the mother, so wala is transferable.
Transferable means the wala can shift to another person if the child is later freed by someone else.
4
Apply the rule to a new scenario
Given a specific situation, use the six-month rule to decide whether the child's wala is transferable. Practice with hypotheticals.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فائدہ دونوں صورتوں میں فرق یہ ہوا کہ پہلی صورت میں جب کہ بوقت اعتاق حمل موجود ہے یا بچہ چھ ماہ سے کم پر جنا جس سے اعتاق کے وقت موجود ہونے کا تیقن ہے تو اس صورت میں بچہ بالقصد آزد کیا گیا ہے اور آزاد کنندہ وہی آتا ہے جس نے اس کی ماں کو آزاد کیا ہے پس آزاد کنندہ سے ولاء منقول نہ ہوگی۔ اور اس دوسری صورت میں جب آزدی کے وقت سے چھ ماہ سے زیادہ پر جنا ہے جس سے بوقت اعتاق حمل موجود ہونے کا تیقین نہیں ہے تو اس صورت میں بچہ کی آزادی قصدا نہ ہوگی بلکہ ماں کی تبعیت میں ہوگی حتی کہ یہ ولاء قابل انتقال ہے۔ اگر چہ با فعل اس کی ولاء ماں کے آقا کے لئے ہوگی۔
Benefit: The difference between the two cases is that in the first case, when the fetus is present at the time of emancipation or the child is born less than six months [after emancipation], so that its existence at the time of emancipation is certain, then in this case the child is freed intentionally, and the emancipator is the same one who freed its mother. Thus wala will not be transferred from the emancipator. In the second case, when it is born more than six months after the time of emancipation, so that there is no certainty of the fetus's existence at the time of emancipation, then in this case the child's freedom is not intentional but follows the mother. Thus this wala is transferable. However, initially its wala belongs to the mother's master.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a ruling explaining the difference between two scenarios regarding the wala of a child born after the mother's emancipation. The key factor is the certainty of the child's existence at the time the mother was freed. If the child was conceived before the emancipation (i.e., born within six months), its existence is certain, and the child is freed intentionally along with the mother. The wala then belongs to the mother's master and is not transferable. If the child is born after six months, it is deemed conceived after the emancipation, so its freedom is not intentional but follows the mother. In that case, the wala is transferable (e.g., if the father later becomes free). This distinction is crucial in Hanafi fiqh for determining the transferability of wala.

Key Terms
ولاء (wala'): The right of inheritance/patronage that a former master holds over a freed slave, and vice versa, affecting inheritance and certain legal relationships.
اعتاق (i'taq): Emancipation or manumission of a slave, which establishes wala for the emancipator.
حمل (haml): Fetus or unborn child.
تبعیت (taba'iyyah): Following; in this context, the child's freedom is subordinate to and derived from the mother's emancipation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which case is the wala of a child born after the mother's emancipation transferable?
A) When the child is born within six months.
B) When the child is born after six months.
C) Always.
D) Never.

Key Takeaway
The transferability of wala for a child born after the mother's emancipation depends on the certainty of the child's existence at the time of emancipation, determined by the six-month gestational rule.

Transfer of Wala from Mother's Patrons to Father's Patrons When Father is Freed
Ruling on father's wala transfer with proof and dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on transfer of wala when the father is freed, and explain the proof and the response to the opposing view.

Core Idea
Wala transfers to the father's patrons because it is like lineage, and the father's eligibility overrides the mother's.

This passage addresses a specific scenario: a child is freed along with his mother, and later the father is freed. The question is whether the wala (patronage) of the child remains with the mother's patrons or transfers to the father's patrons. The Hanafi school, following the majority of Companions and Successors, rules that it transfers, supported by a hadith comparing wala to lineage and an analogy with li'an children.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
The child is freed with the mother (due to her freedom) while the father is still a slave. Later the father is freed. The Hanafi ruling: wala transfers from mother's patrons to father's patrons.
This is not the case where the child is freed directly by a master.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: 'al-wala' luhmah ka luhmah al-nasab' (wala is a bond like the bond of lineage). Since lineage goes to the fathers, so does wala.
The hadith establishes the nature of wala as a kinship-like bond.
3
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars (Malik ibn Aws, Zuhri, Dawud al-Zahiri, etc.) hold that wala does not transfer, arguing that wala is like lineage and once established cannot be removed.
Uthman and Zayd ibn Thabit are also reported to hold this view, but Ibn al-Laban denied that.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes between annulment (which does not happen) and precedence (a stronger wala takes over). Analogy: a brother's asabah is not invalidated but a closer relative takes precedence. Further refinement: wala established due to necessity (like lineage of a li'an child) is non-fixed and can be overridden when the obstacle is removed.
This answers the objection that wala is permanent.

Source Text

ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد ہے الولاء لحمة اھا کہ ولاء ایک قرابت ہے قرابت نسب کی طرح نہ اس کو فروخت کیا جا سکتا ہے نہ ہبہ اور نہ اس میں وراثت جاری ہو سکتی ہے پھر نسب چونکہ بجانب آباء ہوتا ہے۔ تو ایسے ہی ملا ر بھی آباء کی طرف ہو گی ۔ پہلی صورت میں جو نسب موالی ام کی طرف ہو گئی تھی وہ باپ کی عدم اہلبیت کی وجہ سے تھی اور جب باپ میں آزادی کی وجہ سے لیاقت پیدا ہوگئی تو ولا ء اس کی طرف لوٹ آئے گی اس کی نظیر یہ ہے کہ ایک عورت نے شوہر سے ملانہ کیا اور اس سے بچہ پیدا ہوا جو بوجہ ضرورت قوم ام کی طرف منسوب ہو گیا۔ اس کے بعد باپ نے کہا کہ میں اس عورت کو تہمت زنا لگانے میں جھوٹا تھا تو یہ بچہ پھر اپنے باپ کی طرف منسوب ہو جائے گا۔ عبارت " و انتقل عن موالى الام "پر کافی میں ایک اعتراض ذکر کیا ہے اور وہ یہ کہ ولاء نسب کی طرح ہے اور نسب ثابت ہو جانے کے بعد حتمل فتح نہیں ہوتا تو ایسے ہی ولاء بھی ثابت ہو جانے کے بعد فسخ نہیں ہونی چاہیئے ۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ ولاء منح تو نہیں ہوگی ۔ البتہ اس سے بڑھ کر ولا ء پیش آنے کی وجہ سے وہ مقدم ہو جائے گی جیسے بھائی عصبہ ہوتا ہے۔ لیکن جب وراثت میں اُس سے اولی شخص ظاہر ہو جائے تو بھائی کی تعصیب باطل تو نہیں ہوتی مگر وہ شخص اس پر مقدم ہو جاتا ہے۔ یہ سوال و جواب غایہ البیان میں بھی مذکور ہے جو انہوں نے شیخ ابو نصر سے نقل کیا ہے۔ پھر جواب مذکور پر صاحب نتایج نے ایک کال کیا ہے جس کا خاتمہ یوں ہو سکتا ہے کہ نسب کا ثبوت دو طرح کا ہوتا ہے ایک ثبوت محکم اور ایک ثبوت غیر محکم ( جو اصالہ نہ ہو بلکہ امر عارض کی وجہ سے ہو ) ان میں سے ثبوت محکم تو متحمل فسخ نہیں ہوتا ۔ رہا ثبوت غیر محکم سودہ زوال عارض کے وقت متحمل فسخ ہوتا ہے۔ جیسے ابن الملاعنہ کا نسب نقص ملائن کی بنا پر ماں سے ثابت ہو جاتا ہے فکذاثبوت الولاء ۔
If the father is freed, the father draws the wala of his son, and it transfers from the patrons of the mother to the patrons of the father, because here the freedom of the child is established as following the mother, unlike the first case. And this is because wala is like lineage. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: "Wala is a bond like the bond of lineage; it is not sold, nor given as a gift, nor inherited." Then lineage goes to the fathers, so similarly wala. And the attribution to the mother's patrons was due to necessity because of the father's lack of eligibility. So when he becomes eligible, wala returns to him, like the child of a woman who is involved in li'an: due to necessity, it is attributed to the mother's people, but when the one who casts li'an denies himself, it is attributed to him. Translation: Then if he is freed, the father will draw the wala of his son, and it will transfer from the mother's patrons to the father's patrons. Because here the child's freedom is established as a follower of the mother, unlike the first case. And this is because wala is like lineage. The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: "Wala is a kinship like the kinship of lineage; it will not be sold, nor gifted, nor inherited." Then lineage is towards the fathers, so similarly wala. And the attribution to the mother's patrons was due to the father's lack of eligibility out of necessity. When the father becomes eligible, wala returns to him, like the child of a woman involved in li'an: due to necessity, it is attributed to the mother's people, and when the one who casts li'an denies himself, it will be attributed to him. Commentary on his statement 'If the father is freed...': If the child's father is freed, then he will draw the child's wala to himself, and the wala will transfer from the mother's patrons to the father's patrons. The majority of the great Companions and Successors—Umar, Uthman, Ali, Zubayr, Abdullah, Zayd ibn Thabit, and also Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib, Hasan al-Basri, Ibn Sirin, Umar ibn Abd al-Aziz, Ibrahim al-Nakha'i—are reported to hold this view. And Sufyan al-Thawri, Layth ibn Sa'd, Ishaq ibn Rahwayh, Abu Thawr, the Three Imams, and the Hanafis are of the same opinion. Contrary to this, Malik ibn Aws ibn Hadathan, Ibn Shihab al-Zuhri, Dawud al-Zahiri, Maymun ibn Mihran, and Humayd ibn Abd al-Rahman hold that wala does not transfer from the mother's patrons. Uthman and Zayd ibn Thabit are also reported to have a similar view, but Ibn al-Laban denied that. His statement 'because wala is like lineage...': Our evidence is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: "Wala is a bond like the bond of lineage; it cannot be sold, nor gifted, nor inherited." Then lineage is towards the fathers, so similarly wala. In the first case, the lineage had gone to the mother's patrons due to the father's lack of qualifications. When the father becomes qualified due to freedom, wala returns to him. An example is a woman who engaged in li'an with her husband and gave birth to a child, who out of necessity is attributed to the mother's people. Then the father says that he was lying in accusing her of adultery, so the child becomes attributed to his father. On the phrase 'and it transfers from the mother's patrons', in al-Kafi an objection is mentioned: wala is like lineage, and once lineage is established, it cannot be undone; similarly, wala once established should not be annulled. The answer is that wala is not annulled; rather, when a stronger wala appears, it takes precedence, just as a brother is an 'asabah, but when a closer person appears in inheritance, the brother's 'asabah is not invalidated, but that person takes precedence. This question and answer are also mentioned in al-Ghayat al-Bayan, which he narrated from Shaykh Abu Nasr. Then, on the mentioned answer, the author of al-Nata'ij made a remark: the proof of lineage is of two types: a fixed proof and a non-fixed proof (which is not original but due to an incidental matter). Among them, the fixed proof does not allow annulment; as for the non-fixed proof, it allows annulment when the incidental matter ceases. For example, the lineage of a son of li'an is established from the mother based on the accusation; similarly, the proof of wala.
Source pages p. 209

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the transfer of wala when a father is freed after his child has already been freed along with the mother. The Hanafi position is that wala transfers from the mother's patrons to the father's patrons, supported by the hadith that wala is like lineage, and lineage goes to the fathers. The passage provides the proof (hadith), states the majority view (including the four imams), and notes an opposing minority view. It then addresses an objection: if wala is like lineage, it cannot be transferred once established. The answer is that wala is not annulled; rather, a stronger wala takes precedence. The analogy is made with a brother's asabah being overridden by a closer relative. Further refinement: lineage can be of two types (fixed and non-fixed), and the wala in question is of the non-fixed type, thus transferable when the obstacle (father's unfreedom) is removed.

Key Terms
ولاء (wala'): Patronage right of a former master over a freed slave, including inheritance rights.
موالی الام (mawali al-umm): Patrons of the mother; the former masters who hold wala over the mother and thus originally over the child.
موالی الاب (mawali al-ab): Patrons of the father; the former masters who hold wala over the father.
لحمة (luhmah): Bond, tie; used to describe wala as a kinship-like bond.
ملاعنة (mula'anah): Li'an; mutual cursing between spouses leading to separation and denial of paternity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on the transfer of wala when a father is freed after his child?
A) Wala transfers to father's patrons.
B) Wala remains with mother's patrons.
C) Wala is annulled.
D) Wala splits between patrons.

Key Takeaway
Wala transfers to the father's patrons because wala is like lineage and the father's eligibility supersedes the mother's when the father is freed.

6 min
Transfer of Wala When Father Becomes Eligible
Ruling on wala transfer with example

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on transfer of wala when the father's right is established and explain the illustrative example from lineage.

Core Idea
A stronger wala overrides an earlier wala without annulling it.

In the Book of Wala from Al-Hidayah, the author presents a ruling that when a father gains eligibility through manumission, the wala of his child reverts to him. An example from family law—where a child initially attributed to the mother is re-attributed when the father admits paternity—illustrates the principle of transfer upon removal of an obstacle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling on Wala Transfer
Find the sentence stating that wala reverts to the father when eligibility arises due to freedom. This is the core ruling.
The phrase 'لوٹ آئے گی' indicates a return or transfer.
2
Understand the Illustrative Example
Read the example of the quarreling couple and the child's attribution. Note how the child's lineage shifts from the mother's tribe to the father when the father's false accusation is retracted.
This is a parallel to wala: the mother's wala is like the tribe's temporary attribution.
3
Recognize the Analogy Between Wala and Lineage
The author directly compares the transfer of wala to the transfer of lineage. Both involve a prior right being superseded by a stronger claim.
This analogy sets up the later objection and answer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الولاء
اور جب باپ میں آزادی کی وجہ سے لیاقت پیدا ہوگئی تو ولا ء اس کی طرف لوٹ آئے گی اس کی نظیر یہ ہے کہ ایک عورت نے شوہر سے ملانہ کیا اور اس سے بچہ پیدا ہوا جو بوجہ ضرورت قوم ام کی طرف منسوب ہو گیا۔ اس کے بعد باپ نے کہا کہ میں اس عورت کو تہمت زنا لگانے میں جھوٹا تھا تو یہ بچہ پھر اپنے باپ کی طرف منسوب ہو جائے گا۔
عبارت " و انتقل عن موالى الام "پر کافی میں ایک اعتراض ذکر کیا ہے اور وہ یہ کہ ولاء نسب کی طرح ہے اور نسب ثابت ہو
جانے کے بعد حتمل فتح نہیں ہوتا تو ایسے ہی ولاء بھی ثابت ہو جانے کے بعد فسخ نہیں ہونی چاہیئے ۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ ولاء منح تو نہیں ہوگی ۔ البتہ اس سے بڑھ کر ولا ء پیش آنے کی وجہ سے وہ مقدم ہو جائے گی جیسے بھائی عصبہ ہوتا ہے۔ لیکن جب وراثت میں اُس سے اولی شخص ظاہر ہو جائے تو بھائی کی تعصیب باطل تو نہیں ہوتی مگر وہ شخص اس پر مقدم ہو جاتا ہے۔ یہ سوال و جواب غایہ البیان میں بھی مذکور ہے جو انہوں نے شیخ ابو نصر سے نقل کیا ہے۔
پھر جواب مذکور پر صاحب نتایج نے ایک کال کیا ہے جس کا خاتمہ یوں ہو سکتا ہے کہ نسب کا ثبوت دو طرح کا ہوتا ہے ایک ثبوت محکم اور ایک ثبوت غیر محکم ( جو اصالہ نہ ہو بلکہ امر عارض کی وجہ سے ہو ) ان میں سے ثبوت محکم تو متحمل فسخ نہیں ہوتا ۔ رہا ثبوت غیر محکم سودہ زوال عارض کے وقت متحمل فسخ ہوتا ہے۔ جیسے ابن الملاعنہ کا نسب نقی ملائن کی بنا پر ماں سے ثابت ہو جاتا ہے فکذاثبوت الولاء ۔
Book of Wala. And when eligibility arises in the father due to freedom, wala will revert to him. Its example is that a woman quarreled with her husband, and a child was born who, due to necessity, was attributed to the tribe of the mother. Then the father said: I was false in accusing this woman of adultery, so this child will again be attributed to his father. On the phrase 'and it transfers from the clients of the mother', an objection is mentioned in al-Kafi: wala is like lineage, and lineage once established cannot be rescinded, so wala also should not be rescinded after establishment. The answer: Wala will not be rescinded. Rather, due to a stronger wala appearing, it will take precedence, just as a brother is an asabah, but when a person closer in inheritance appears, the brother's asabah is not annulled but that person takes precedence. This question and answer are also mentioned in Ghayat al-Bayan, which they narrated from Shaykh Abu Nasr. Then the author of Nata'ij made a remark on the mentioned answer, whose conclusion is: The proof of lineage is of two types: one strong proof and one weak proof (which is not original but due to an incidental cause). Among them, the strong proof cannot tolerate rescission. As for the weak proof, it tolerates rescission when the incidental cause is removed, like the lineage of the child of li'an is established from the mother on the basis of li'an. Similarly is the proof of wala.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage discusses the transfer of wala (clientage) when the father's right becomes effective. The author gives an example: a woman accuses her husband of lying about paternity, and the child is attributed to the mother. When the father admits, the child is re-attributed to the father. Similarly, wala transfers to the father when he becomes eligible due to manumission. An objection from Kafi states that wala is like lineage and once established cannot be rescinded. The response explains that wala is not rescinded but overridden by a stronger wala, just as a brother's asabah is not annulled but superseded by a closer relative. Then Nata'ij refines: lineage can be strong (muhkam) or weak (ghayr muhkam). Weak lineage, established due to an obstacle, can be rescinded when the obstacle is removed, like the child of li'an. Similarly, wala established due to a temporary cause can be overridden.

Key Terms
ولاء (wala): Clientage: the right of inheritance and guardianship between a freed slave and the manumitter.
تعصیب (ta'sib): The status of being an asabah (residuary heir) by virtue of being a male agnate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, what happens to the mother's clients' wala when the father becomes eligible?
A) It is completely annulled.
B) It is overridden and becomes dormant.
C) It remains and both wala rights are equal.
D) It transfers intact to the father.

Key Takeaway
When a stronger wala appears, it overrides the earlier wala without annulling it, like a closer relative superseding a brother's asabah.

8 min
Objection and Answer: Wala is Overridden, Not Rescinded
Objection and answer on wala transfer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the objection that wala cannot be rescinded and the Hanafi response using the analogy of asabah, including the refinement distinguishing strong and weak proof.

Core Idea
Wala is not rescinded but overridden; weak lineage can be rescinded when the obstacle is removed.

The author of Hidayah presents an objection from the Kafi: since wala is like lineage and lineage cannot be rescinded, how can wala be transferred? The answer relies on a qiyas to asabah: the brother's asabah is not annulled but superseded. A later scholar (Nata'ij) refines this by distinguishing between strong and weak lineage proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection from Al-Kafi
Read the objection: if wala is like lineage, and lineage cannot be rescinded, then wala should not be rescinded either.
The key word is 'la yah tamallu faskh' (cannot be rescinded).
2
Analyze the Answer Using Asabah Analogy
The author replies that wala is not rescinded but takes precedence. He compares it to a brother's asabah: although the brother is an asabah, when a closer relative appears, the brother's asabah is not annulled; the closer one takes precedence.
This is a clear qiyas: wala is the far', asabah is the asl.
3
Examine the Refinement by Nata'ij
The author of Nata'ij adds: there are two types of proof of lineage: strong (muhkam) and weak (ghayr muhkam). Weak lineage, like that of the child of li'an, can be rescinded when the obstacle is removed. Wala is like weak lineage because it was established due to an obstacle (father's slavery).
This refinement explains why wala can be overridden: it was never a strong right to begin with.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

اور جب باپ میں آزادی کی وجہ سے لیاقت پیدا ہوگئی تو ولا ء اس کی طرف لوٹ آئے گی اس کی نظیر یہ ہے کہ ایک عورت نے شوہر سے ملانہ کیا اور اس سے بچہ پیدا ہوا جو بوجہ ضرورت قوم ام کی طرف منسوب ہو گیا۔ اس کے بعد باپ نے کہا کہ میں اس عورت کو تہمت زنا لگانے میں جھوٹا تھا تو یہ بچہ پھر اپنے باپ کی طرف منسوب ہو جائے گا۔
عبارت " و انتقل عن موالى الام "پر کافی میں ایک اعتراض ذکر کیا ہے اور وہ یہ کہ ولاء نسب کی طرح ہے اور نسب ثابت ہو
جانے کے بعد حتمل فتح نہیں ہوتا تو ایسے ہی ولاء بھی ثابت ہو جانے کے بعد فسخ نہیں ہونی چاہیئے ۔ جواب یہ ہے کہ ولاء منح تو نہیں ہوگی ۔ البتہ اس سے بڑھ کر ولا ء پیش آنے کی وجہ سے وہ مقدم ہو جائے گی جیسے بھائی عصبہ ہوتا ہے۔ لیکن جب وراثت میں اُس سے اولی شخص ظاہر ہو جائے تو بھائی کی تعصیب باطل تو نہیں ہوتی مگر وہ شخص اس پر مقدم ہو جاتا ہے۔ یہ سوال و جواب غایہ البیان میں بھی مذکور ہے جو انہوں نے شیخ ابو نصر سے نقل کیا ہے۔
پھر جواب مذکور پر صاحب نتایج نے ایک کال کیا ہے جس کا خاتمہ یوں ہو سکتا ہے کہ نسب کا ثبوت دو طرح کا ہوتا ہے ایک ثبوت محکم اور ایک ثبوت غیر محکم ( جو اصالہ نہ ہو بلکہ امر عارض کی وجہ سے ہو ) ان میں سے ثبوت محکم تو متحمل فسخ نہیں ہوتا ۔ رہا ثبوت غیر محکم سودہ زوال عارض کے وقت متحمل فسخ ہوتا ہے۔ جیسے ابن الملاعنہ کا نسب نقی ملائن کی بنا پر ماں سے ثابت ہو جاتا ہے فکذاثبوت الولاء ۔
Book of Wala. And when eligibility arises in the father due to freedom, wala will revert to him. Its example is that a woman quarreled with her husband, and a child was born who, due to necessity, was attributed to the tribe of the mother. Then the father said: I was false in accusing this woman of adultery, so this child will again be attributed to his father. Commentary
This passage discusses the transfer of wala (clientage) when the father's right becomes effective. The author gives an example: a woman accuses her husband of lying about paternity, and the child is attributed to the mother. When the father admits, the child is re-attributed to the father. Similarly, wala transfers to the father when he becomes eligible due to manumission. An objection from Kafi states that wala is like lineage and once established cannot be rescinded. The response explains that wala is not rescinded but overridden by a stronger wala, just as a brother's asabah is not annulled but superseded by a closer relative. Then Nata'ij refines: lineage can be strong (muhkam) or weak (ghayr muhkam). Weak lineage, established due to an obstacle, can be rescinded when the obstacle is removed, like the child of li'an. Similarly, wala established due to a temporary cause can be overridden.

Key Terms
منع (man'): Prevention, not annulment; the earlier wala is prevented from taking effect, not erased.
ثبوت محکم (thubut muhkam): Strong proof that is permanent and cannot be rescinded.
ثبوت غیر محکم (thubut ghayr muhkam): Weak proof that is due to an incidental cause and can be rescinded when the cause is removed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main argument in the answer to the objection in al-Kafi?
A) Wala is not like lineage; it is completely different.
B) Wala is not rescinded but overridden, like a brother's asabah being superseded by a closer relative.
C) Wala can be rescinded if both parties agree.
D) Wala is a weak right and can be annulled freely.

Key Takeaway
The objection that wala cannot be rescinded is answered by distinguishing override from rescission and by recognizing that weak proofs (like wala) can be superseded when the obstacle is removed.

Hadith Proofs that Wala is Non-Transferable
Discussion of hadiths proving wala is like lineage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the transferability of wala and cite the primary hadith proof that establishes its non-transferability.

Core Idea
Wala is a bond like lineage; cannot be sold, gifted, or inherited.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah delves into the hadith evidence underpinning the Hanafi ruling that wala (clientage) is a non-transferable legal relationship. The commentary traces multiple hadith narrations to establish that wala is akin to lineage (nasab) and therefore cannot be treated as property. Understanding these proofs is essential for grasping the nature of wala as a right of 'asabah, not a commodity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on wala (clientage) and states it cannot be sold, gifted, or inherited. Identify the precise hukm level (haram) for the acts of selling or gifting wala.
The ruling is based on explicit prophetic prohibition.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The primary dalil is the hadith: 'Wala is a bond like the bond of lineage; it is not sold nor gifted.' Identify the chain and its takhrij as discussed in the commentary.
Multiple narrations are cited from Ibn 'Umar, Ibn Abi Awfa, Abu Hurayrah, and 'Ali (may Allah be pleased with them).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the hadith proves the ruling: the explicit words 'la yuba' wa la yuhab' directly forbid sale and gift. The analogy to lineage (lahmah) indicates permanence and non-transferability.
The Hanafi school considers this dalala as qat'i (definitive) in meaning.
4
Evaluate the hadith authenticity
Note the discussion on the strength of each chain. Hafiz Ibn Hajar considers the hadith of Ibn Abi Awfa 'apparently authentic' (zahir al-sanad al-sihhah), while al-Bayhaqi considered other chains weak. Understand why the Hanafi school relies on this narration.
The commentary shows the hadith is accepted despite some weak chains.
5
Note the practical implication
The ruling means that wala is not property; it remains with the master and cannot be transferred by any contract. It is inherited by the master's 'asabah, but not as a commodity.
This distinguishes wala from other rights that can be transferred.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا
۲۱۱
كتاب الولاء
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ۱۲ ہے۔ اس میں یہ موجود ہے فانه قال : " لا يباع الولاء يوهب ولا يورث نیز روایت محمد بن اسمعیل الفارسي عن الثورى عن عبد اللہ مین دینار عن ابن عمر بھی یونہی ہے، یہ کل تفصیل حدیث ابن عمر سے متعلق ہے۔ حدیث ابن ابی اوفی کی تخریج (بقول حافظ ابن حجر ) بوجعفر ابن جریر طبری نے تہذیب الاثار میں ۔ حافظ ابونعیم نے معرفۃ الصحابہ میں طبرانی نے معجم کبیر میں ( اور بقول زیلعی ، ابن عدی نے الکامل میں) کی ہے قال رسول الله الولاء لحمة كلحمة النسب لا يباع ولا یو هب حافظ ابن حجر نے تلخیص میں اس حدیث کی بابت و ظاهر اسناده الصحة “ کہنے کے بعد یہ بھی کہا ہے بنکر على البهيقى حيث قال عقیب حدیث ابی یوسف "يروى بأسانيدا آخر كلها ضعيفة “ حدیث ابوہریرہ کی تخریج ابن عدی نے الکامل میں کی ہے لیکن اس کا راوی بھی بن ابی انیسہ متروک ہے، چنانچہ ابن عدی نے ، امام بخاری ، نسائی امام احمد ابن المدینی اور ابن معین سے اس کی تضعیف نقل کی ہے اور کہا ہے کہ اس کا بھائی زید بن ابی انیسہ ثقہ ہے۔ حدیث علی کو حافظ بیہقی نے سنن میں باب کے آخر میں ذکر کر کے کوئی علت ذکر نہیں کی۔ اور نہ شیخ ابن الترکمانی صاحب الجو ہر انفی نے کوئی علت ذکر کی۔
[Page margin: no, 211] Book of Wala. This is Ashraf al-Hidaya, an Urdu commentary on al-Hidaya, volume 12. In it is present that he said: 'Wala is not sold, nor gifted, nor inherited.' Also the narration of Muhammad ibn Isma'il al-Farisi from al-Thawri from 'Abdullah ibn Dinar from Ibn 'Umar is likewise. All this detail relates to the hadith of Ibn 'Umar. The takhrij of the hadith of Ibn Abi Awfa (according to Hafiz Ibn Hajar) is by Ja'far ibn Jarir al-Tabari in Tahdhib al-Athar, by Hafiz Abu Nu'aym in Ma'rifat al-Sahabah, by al-Tabarani in al-Mu'jam al-Kabir (and according to Zayla'i, by Ibn 'Adi in al-Kamil). The Messenger of Allah said: 'Wala is a bond like the bond of lineage; it is not sold nor gifted.' Hafiz Ibn Hajar, after saying in al-Talkhis regarding this hadith, 'Its chain of transmission is apparently authentic,' also said, objecting to al-Bayhaqi who said after the hadith of Abu Yusuf: 'It is narrated with other chains, all of them weak.' The takhrij of the hadith of Abu Hurayrah is by Ibn 'Adi in al-Kamil, but its narrator, also Ibn Abi Anisah, is matruk. Thus, Ibn 'Adi narrated its weakening from Imam al-Bukhari, al-Nasa'i, Imam Ahmad, Ibn al-Madini, and Ibn Ma'in, and said that his brother, Zayd ibn Abi Anisah, is trustworthy. The hadith of 'Ali was mentioned by Hafiz al-Bayhaqi in al-Sunan at the end of the chapter without mentioning any defect, nor did Shaykh Ibn al-Turkumani, author of al-Jawhar al-[?] Inafi, mention any defect.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It opens with the statement that wala (clientage) is not sold, gifted, or inherited, citing a hadith from Ibn 'Umar. The commentary then provides takhrij (source verification) for several hadiths supporting this ruling: the hadith of Ibn 'Umar via multiple chains, the hadith of Ibn Abi Awfa with the explicit wording 'Wala is a bond like the bond of lineage; it is not sold nor gifted,' the hadith of Abu Hurayrah, and the hadith of 'Ali. The author discusses the authenticity of these narrations, noting that according to Hafiz Ibn Hajar, the hadith of Ibn Abi Awfa has an apparently authentic chain (zahir al-sanad al-sihhah), contra al-Bayhaqi. The hadith of Abu Hurayrah is weakened because of a matruk narrator (Ibn Abi Anisah), while the hadith of 'Ali is mentioned by al-Bayhaqi without any defect. The key point is that wala is a personal legal relationship, akin to lineage, and therefore cannot be transferred by sale, gift, or inheritance. This is a fundamental principle in Hanafi fiqh: wala is a right of 'asabah, not a commodity.

Key Terms
الولاء (al-wala'): The right of inheritance and responsibility for blood money that arises between a patron (master) and a freed slave (client) due to emancipation.
لحمة (lahmah): Bond, tie, relationship; here used metaphorically for a legal connection akin to blood relation.
تخریج (takhrij): The process of tracing a hadith to its original sources and evaluating its chain of transmission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith quoted in this passage, what is wala compared to?
A) Property
B) Lineage (nasab)
C) Debt
D) Marriage

Key Takeaway
Wala is a personal legal relationship akin to lineage, and therefore cannot be sold, gifted, or inherited as property.

Child Born to a Freedwoman in Iddah: Wala to Mother's Patrons
Ruling with proof on wala of a child born to a freedwoman in iddah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wala when a child is born to a freedwoman in iddah within two years, and explain the proof based on the impossibility of attributing pregnancy to the period after death or divorce.

Core Idea
Wala of child born within two years belongs to mother's patrons, even if father freed later.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a nuanced ruling in Hanafi wala law. When a slave woman in iddah is freed and later gives birth within two years of the death or divorce, the child's wala (patronage) belongs to her former masters. The reasoning pivots on the impossibility of attributing the pregnancy to the period after the marital event, due to the prohibition of intercourse. The father's subsequent freedom does not alter this outcome, illustrating the school's careful application of istihsan and legal causation.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its conditions
Identify the essential elements: a woman in iddah of death or divorce is freed, she gives birth within two years of the death/divorce. The child's wala goes to the mother's patrons.
Note that the father's later freedom does not change the ruling.
2
Understand the proof
The proof is based on the impossibility of attributing the formation of the child (علوق) to after death or divorce. After death, intercourse is impossible; after irrevocable divorce, it is prohibited; after revocable divorce, it is doubtful. Therefore, the child is attributed to the marriage period, meaning the child existed at the time of the mother's emancipation.
This is an application of istihsan, preferring attribution to a time when intercourse was lawful.
3
Recognize the contrast case
The passage contrasts this with an earlier scenario where the mother gives birth more than six months after her own emancipation. There, the father's later freedom can draw wala to his patrons.
The difference hinges on whether the child was 'existing' at the moment of the mother's emancipation.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam al-Tahawi restricted the ruling to irrevocable divorce only, while the Hidayah and Hakim al-Shahid left it absolute. The mufta bihi is the absolute position.
The fa'idah section of the text records this difference; the majority view is relied upon.

آزاد کر دی گئی یا وہ طلاق کی عدت گزار رہی تھی ( طلاق بائنہ ہو یا جعی ) کہ اس کو آزاد کر دیا گیا۔ پھر وقت موت یا وقت طلاق سے دو برس سے کم میں بچہ پیدا ہوا تو یہ بچہ اپنی ماں کے موالی کا ہوگا۔ اگر چہ باپ آزاد کر دیا جائے۔ وجہ یہ ہے کہ (موت کی صورت میں ) قرار نطفہ کی اضافت ما بعد الموت کی طرف متعذر ہے۔ یعنی موت کے بعد نطفہ قائم ہونے کا حکم نہیں کر سکتے ۔ کیونکہ یہ میت سے محال ہے اور طلاق بائن کی صورت میں بھی ) قرار نطفہ کی اضافت ما بعد الطلاق البائن کی طرف تعذر ہے۔ کیونکہ طلاق بائن کے بعد وطی حرام ہے۔ نیز طلاق رجعی کے بعد بھی قرار نطفہ کا حکم معذ رہے۔ کیونکہ وہ شک کے ساتھ رجعت کنندہ ہو جاتا ہے (اس لئے کہ اگر اس کو زمانہ عدت کی وطی پر محمول کیا جائے تو رجعت کنندہ ہوتا ہے اور اگر قبل از طلاق پر محمول کیا جائے تو رجعت کنندہ نہیں ہوتا ) حالانکہ شک کے ساتھ رجعت کا ثبوت نہیں ہوتا ۔ تو لا محالہ اس کا استنادات نکاح کی طرف ہوگا۔ پس آزاد کرنے کے وقت بچہ موجود ہوا ۔ لہذا اس کا اعتاق بالقصد واقع ہوگا۔ اور جب اعتماق بالقصد واقع ہوا تو ولاء موالی ام سے منتقل نہیں ہوسکتی۔
فائدہ صاحب ہدایہ نے " عن موت او طلاق میں طلاق کو اس لئے مطلق رکھا ہے تا کہ یہ بائن اور رجعی ہر دو کو شامل رہے۔ حاکم شہید نے بھی یونہی مطلق رکھا ہے۔ البتہ امام طحاوی نے اپنی مختصر میں اس کو بائن کے ساتھ مقید کیا ہے۔ اور شیخ اسیحابی نے اپنی شرح میں انہی کی پیروی کی ہے۔
A woman in iddah of death or divorce was freed; she gave birth to a child in less than two years from the time of death or divorce. This child will be the client of the mother's patrons, even if the father is freed. Contrary to when a woman in iddah of death or divorce is freed and then gives birth to a child in less than two years from the time of death or divorce, where the child is a client of the mother's patrons, even if the father is freed, because attributing the pregnancy to after death or irrevocable divorce is impossible due to the prohibition of intercourse, and after revocable divorce because he becomes a revocator with doubt, so it is attributed to the state of marriage, so the child existed at the time of emancipation and was freed intentionally. Translation: Contrary to when a woman in iddah of death or divorce is freed, then she gives birth to a child in less than two years from the time of death or divorce, that this child will be a client of the mother's patrons, even if the father is freed. Because attributing the pregnancy to after death or irrevocable divorce is impossible due to prohibition, and after revocable divorce also impossible because he becomes a revocator with doubt. So it is attributed to marriage, so at the time of emancipation the child existed, thus he was freed intentionally. Commentary: The statement 'Contrary to when she is freed...' etc. - In al-Nihayah and Miraj al-Dirayah etc. it is that the phrase 'contrary to when she is freed' is connected to the previous statement 'when he becomes eligible, wala returns to him'. The meaning is that if the aforementioned slave woman gives birth more than six months after her emancipation, then the father is freed, he will draw the wala of his child from the mother's patrons to his own patrons. Contrary to the case mentioned in this statement, where he cannot draw the wala of his child to his own patrons, even if the child's birth is more than six months after the mother's emancipation. Rather, the child's wala belongs to the mother's patrons, even if the father is freed. Now first understand the scenario of the disputed case. The case is that a slave woman was the wife of a mukatab. The mukatab died leaving property sufficient to pay the kitabah, and the slave woman was freed, or she was observing the iddah of divorce (irrevocable or revocable) and was freed. Then within less than two years from the time of death or divorce, a child was born. So this child will belong to the mother's patrons, even if the father is freed. The reason is: (in case of death) attributing the formation of the child to after death is impossible, meaning we cannot rule that the child was formed after death, because that is impossible from a dead person. And (in case of irrevocable divorce) attributing the formation of the child to after irrevocable divorce is impossible because intercourse after irrevocable divorce is prohibited. Also after revocable divorce, the ruling of the formation of the child is problematic because he becomes a revocator with doubt (because if it is attributed to intercourse during the iddah period, he is a revocator; if attributed to before divorce, he is not a revocator), since a revocator is not confirmed with doubt. So necessarily it is attributed to the marriage. Thus at the time of emancipation the child existed, so his emancipation occurred intentionally. And when emancipation occurred intentionally, wala cannot be transferred from the mother's patrons. Benefit: The author of al-Hidayah left 'divorce' absolute in 'from death or divorce' so that it includes both irrevocable and revocable. Al-Hakim al-Shahid also left it absolute. However, Imam al-Tahawi restricted it to irrevocable in his Mukhtasar, and Shaykh Aslahabi followed him in his commentary.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, presenting a detailed case in the law of wala. The ruling states: If a slave woman who is in iddah (waiting period) due to the death of her husband or divorce is freed, and she gives birth to a child within two years from the time of death or divorce, the child's wala belongs to the mother's patrons (former masters) even if the father is later freed. The reason is that the pregnancy cannot be attributed to after death or after divorce because intercourse is either impossible (death) or prohibited (irrevocable divorce) or doubtful (revocable divorce). Therefore, the child is considered to have existed at the moment of the mother's emancipation, and since the mother was freed intentionally (not as a consequence of the child's birth), the child's wala does not transfer to the father's patrons if the father is freed later. The commentary elaborates that this contrasts with the earlier case where the mother gives birth more than six months after her own emancipation—there the father's later emancipation would draw the child's wala to his patrons. The benefit (fa'idah) notes a difference of opinion: Imam al-Tahawi restricts 'divorce' to irrevocable, while the Hidayah and Hakim al-Shahid leave it general to include both types. The proof here is based on istihsan and the impossibility of attributing pregnancy to a time when sexual relations are impossible or prohibited.

Key Terms
عدت (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death of husband before remarriage.
علوق ('aluq): Pregnancy, the formation of the child (literally 'clinging' of the embryo).
موالی (mawali): Patrons, the former masters who have the right of wala over a freed slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The child's wala belongs to the mother's patrons when born within two years of death/divorce because the pregnancy cannot be attributed to the post-event period.

Child of a Freedwoman: Wala and Blood Money
Ruling from al-Jami' al-Saghir on intersection of wala and blood money

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the mother's patrons bear the blood money for children of a freedwoman married to a slave and cannot recover it from the father's 'aqila after his emancipation.

Core Idea
Wala is not retroactive: mother's patrons keep the loss when father is freed later.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario from al-Jami' al-Saghir: a freedwoman marries a slave, has free children, and later the father is freed. When the children commit a crime requiring blood money, who pays? The answer hinges on the nature of wala transfer. The ruling uses an analogy to the child of li'an but distinguishes on the basis of retroactivity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Scenario and Initial Ruling
State the situation: freedwoman married to a slave, children born free. If they commit a crime, the blood money is on the mother's patrons because the children have no other 'aqila.
Children are free because they follow their mother in emancipation.
2
Understand the Analogy to Child of Li'an
Note that the mother's patrons bear the blood money out of necessity, similar to how the mother's people bear it for a child of li'an where paternity is denied.
In both cases, the mother's side acts as 'aqila by default.
3
Analyze the Distinction When Father is Freed
When the father is later freed, he draws the wala of the children to himself. However, the mother's patrons cannot recover the blood money they paid from his 'aqila.
The key is timing: the payment occurred when wala belonged to the mother's patrons.
4
Contrast with Child of Li'an
In the li'an case, if the father later admits paternity, the mother's people can recover from him because lineage is established retroactively. In the wala case, the father's wala is only prospective.
Lineage retroactivity vs. wala prospectivity is the distinguishing factor.
5
State the Final Ruling
The mother's patrons cannot seek reimbursement because at the time of payment, wala was theirs; the father's later wala does not reverse past obligations.
This is the Hanafi position from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: If a freedwoman marries a slave and gives birth to children, then the children commit a crime (a sin that incurs blood money), then their blood money is upon the mother's patrons because they were freed as a consequence of their mother, and they have no 'aqila (subsidiary group responsible for blood money) from their father nor patrons, so they are attached to the mother's patrons out of necessity, as in the case of a child of li'an (imprecation) as we have mentioned. Then if the father is freed, he draws the wala of the children to himself as we explained, but they (the mother's patrons) cannot recover from the father's 'aqila what they paid, because when they paid, the wala was established for them, and for the father it is established restrictively (only future) because its cause (emancipation) is restrictive. Contrary to the case of the child of li'an, when the mother's people pay the blood money for him, then the one who performed li'an contradicts himself (i.e., admits paternity), where they can recover from him, because there lineage is established retroactively to the time of conception, and they were compelled to pay, so they can recover. Translation: In al-Jami' al-Saghir: If a freedwoman marries a slave and gives birth to children, then the children commit a crime, so their blood money is upon the mother's patrons because these children were freed as a consequence of their mother, and their father has no 'aqila or patrons. So out of necessity they are attached to the mother's patrons, as in the case of a child of li'an. Then if the father is freed, he draws the wala of the children to himself, and the mother's patrons cannot recover from the father's 'aqila what they paid. Because when they paid the blood money, wala was established for them, and for the father it is established restrictively (only future), because its cause (emancipation) is restrictive. Contrary to the case of a child of li'an, when the mother's people pay the blood money for him, then the one who performed li'an contradicts himself (i.e., admits paternity), then they can recover from him, because there lineage is established retroactively to the time of conception, and they were compelled to pay, so they can recover.
